Shanghai Import Industry Already Affected by North China Smuggling

Report by the Correspondent of the English-Language Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury

According to the English-Language Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury, translated by a foreign news agency, a correspondent for the Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury investigated the impact of smuggling on the Shanghai market. The investigation found that the number of smuggled goods entering the concession market from both North and South China is increasing daily. Due to the competition from smuggled goods, reputable local merchants are gradually losing their customers in other areas. Transactions in several regions have even completely ceased. When the correspondent interviewed various merchants to inquire about the current state of smuggling, their managers and staff appeared extremely resentful. Their replies to the correspondent were generally as follows: "We have no statistics, so we cannot clearly tell you the quantity of smuggled goods. However, we can state definitively that this smuggling is dealing a tremendous blow to legitimate importers." When the correspondent inquired about the true impact on Shanghai's import industry, it was reported that the goods currently entering the concession market in the largest quantities are various high-value items that are easy to conceal, such as rayon fabrics, cosmetics, and medicinal materials. Other bulky goods, such as canned foods, paper, cloth, and manufactured goods in boxes, are flowing into the interior in large quantities, causing Shanghai's merchants to completely lose their original transactions. Furthermore, many products from major companies are being transported from Tianjin to Shanghai via railways, leading to a phenomenon of oversupply in the market. Last week, at least 500 boxes of American-branded condensed milk were smuggled into Shanghai, with purchase prices far lower than local selling prices. There are now widespread rumors that large quantities of white sugar are also being shipped in the same way. However, the exact quantity is currently unknown. Because tariffs on certain goods, such as sugar and silk, are very high, smugglers are focusing their activities on these items. However, local importers believe that as large quantities of smuggled goods enter the market, creating an oversupply of inventory, it is only a matter of time before this illegal business faces the same difficulties as legitimate trade. In fact, the only import businesses currently unaffected by smuggled goods are heavy machinery, steel, iron, and certain specialty items ordered directly from merchants here. Foreign manufacturers have not suffered significant damage, as many commercial nations other than Japan also ship goods to free ports. The hardest hit are local importers and the Chinese Customs. Importers believe that if the government could reduce tariffs to 5% ad valorem, revenue would likely increase compared to today. A representative of a foreign trading company stated, "If customs can lower its tariffs, Japan's tactics can be defeated in ten minutes." He added that those who blame the Japanese authorities for condoning their nationals' involvement in smuggling should instead focus on the Chinese Customs, as they are responsible for raising tariffs. Another foreign merchant expressed the opinion that in May 1933, the import tax on certain luxury goods, such as diamonds, was reduced, while the tax rate on several necessities, such as hardware and food, was increased, which was inappropriate. The current rampant smuggling is also related to this. According to a clothing merchant who spoke to the correspondent, women's clothing tailors in the French Concession have received a considerable number of smuggled goods in the past two to three months, with a large quantity expected soon. Silk that sold for two yuan per yard last winter has now fallen to 75 cents per yard, with a continued price decrease expected. A merchant also reported, "Shanghai used to be the central hub for stocking imports. However, the situation has changed dramatically. Ship crews traveling between Shanghai, Hong Kong, and other ports are smuggling large quantities of stocking, profiting greatly, more than their salaries. The import tax on stockings in Shanghai is 100%. When these ship crews arrive in Shanghai, they hide the stockings in their clothes, and no one can detect them upon landing." A local merchant recently returned from traveling to various ports in North and Central China and stated that smuggled goods, aided by the opening of the Canton-Hankow Railway, are likely to spread throughout the country. The manager of a large general merchandise trading company stated that their business has been affected in two ways. First, their Tianjin branch. Previously, general merchandise stores in Tianjin would purchase goods from Shanghai. However, since the start of smuggling, all business has completely disappeared. Second, certain goods sold by their company are, in fact, being smuggled to various regions. There are recent rumors that several import merchants in Shanghai may also order their goods through the Dalian Free Port. However, before taking such action, they are willing to fight against the high tariffs here. However, they know that this effort is unlikely to be successful. A paper merchant stated that they currently have no transactions in North China. The reason why the local market has not yet been affected is that large quantities of paper are too bulky and difficult to smuggle. However, it is only a matter of time before they are affected. A foreign merchant engaged in the packing business recently returned from Tianjin and reported that all commercial activity in North China has come to a standstill. In order to sell their goods, merchants are reducing prices and extending credit for one month. Several large Chinese stores have gone bankrupt due to the market conditions. In the first three months of this year, goods imported into China decreased by 51 million yuan compared to the same period last year. The largest decrease was in Tianjin, from 21,800,000 yuan to 11,900,000 yuan. In recent months, large quantities of raw silk and rayon have been smuggled into Shanghai. The exact amount is still unknown. The smuggling methods are quite ingenious, often beyond expectations. From January to April last year, the import value of raw silk and silk fabrics was 2,300,000 yuan. During the same period this year, the total has fallen to 1,500,000 yuan. The decline after April will be even more alarming. In the first three months of 1935, China's imports of silk products from Italy were worth 600,000 gold standard yuan. During the same period this year, it has fallen to below 300,000 gold standard yuan. Goods exported from Japan have also fallen from 473,000 gold standard yuan to 270,000 gold standard yuan. According to Sir Shalita's estimates, the tax revenue lost by China at the Meiguan customs checkpoint is about 25% to 30%. In reality, the amount of goods smuggled into China is 15% to 20% higher than previously recorded. Customs officials are well aware that to prevent smuggling on a large scale, only two methods can be adopted: 1. Reduce tariffs to make smuggling less attractive. 2. Increase anti-smuggling efforts to make smuggling extremely difficult. The main imports susceptible to smuggling are diamonds, gems, jewelry, shark fins, bird's nests, ginseng, white sugar, rayon, woolen fabrics, and silk fabrics. Customs officials are making great efforts to prevent smuggling. Anti-smuggling personnel are stationed along the coast for inspection, and patrol ships are constantly patrolling the sea.

20th International Labour Conference Chinese Labour Representatives' Proposals

Request the Formulation of a Convention on Equal Treatment of Chinese and Foreign Workers, Establishment of a Mutual Aid System, and Compliance with Labour Laws; Suggest the Conference Assist China in Prohibiting Opium and Narcotics

Dagon News Agency: The 20th International Labour Conference is scheduled to be held in Geneva on June 4th. The labour representative appointed by the Chinese government, Zhu Xuefan, and the employer representative, Sun Fangyu, have departed to attend. The proposals from the Chinese labour side for this Conference total four, all translated by Mr. Zhu into various languages and submitted to the Conference for discussion, striving for their realization. The full text is excerpted below:

Regarding the issue of equal treatment for domestic and foreign workers, request the Conference to decide to include it on the agenda of the most recent Conference and to formulate a public draft as soon as possible. (Explanation) Regarding the issue of equal treatment for domestic and foreign workers, the 17th International Labour Conference in 1933 passed the following resolution: "Recognizing the importance of the protection afforded to workers employed abroad by Part XIII of the Treaty of Versailles and other problem sections of peace treaties, and for the full implementation of the recommendation 'Concerning Reciprocity of Treatment of Foreign Workers and Their Families and Domestic Workers' passed by the First International Labour Conference held in Washington in 1919," "Recognizing that the 12th International Labour Conference has requested the Governing Body of the International Labour Office to note the necessity of including this issue on the agenda of the most recent International Labour Conference," "Recognizing that the world has long suffered from financial and economic panic, and the treatment of workers residing abroad violates the principles of equality and justice, with many workers being forced to leave their country of employment, leading to displacement and hardship," "And recognizing that the Migration Committee of the International Labour Office has begun to study the issue of equal treatment, the 17th International Labour Conference specifically requests the Governing Body to consider the necessity of implementing existing research, and to include this issue on the agenda of the most recent International Labour Conference, in order that this issue may be formulated into a public convention as soon as possible. The importance of this issue and the urgency of its resolution have been acknowledged by the Conference. The severity of the current global economic panic is more profound than when the above resolution was passed. Foreign workers residing in various countries suffer discrimination and exclusion from the host government, making survival impossible, violating principles of fairness and humanity. The repeated occurrence of such injustices poses a major crisis to human peace. Request the Conference to decide to include the resolution passed by the 17th Conference on the agenda of the most recent International Labour Conference, and to formulate a public draft to alleviate the legal and social oppression suffered by overseas workers. Request the International Labour Conference to instruct the Governing Body to contact the governments of all member states to establish an international mutual aid system for labour employment services, to alleviate unemployment. (Explanation) Currently, public employment service systems seem to be universally implemented in various countries, and there are also many employment service agencies organized by private groups. However, all are limited to within the country. There is no establishment of such joint organizations or liaison systems internationally. Based on past experience, labour supply and demand situations vary greatly between countries. Often, one country lacks certain talents and cannot find them, while another country suffers from an excess of certain talents and struggles to place them. Due to geographical relations, information is isolated, and both parties cannot mutually satisfy their needs. There is also an illegal labour recruitment system, where privately operated recruitment agencies exploit workers' ignorance and sign extremely harsh contracts with workers, forcing them to engage in inhumane work or restricting their freedom. Countless workers are harmed by this system. If an international mutual aid system for labour employment services could be established, or a permanent international labour employment service agency could be established, regularly handling international employment service information, investigation, statistics, contact, guidance, and other work, the above shortcomings and malpractices could be prevented, which would have a very significant effect on resolving the unemployment problem. The global unemployment panic is becoming increasingly serious, and this issue deserves consideration. Regarding the implementation methods of this system, please first seek opinions from all members of the Council before making a decision. Request the Conference to recommend that the governments of all member states allow all factories established in China to comply with Chinese labour laws and allow Chinese workers to enjoy the right to assembly and association. (Explanation) The purpose of labour legislation is to protect the safety and happiness of workers, entirely to maintain human peace. The Chinese government has attached great importance to labour legislation in recent years. Laws such as the "Factory Law," "Trade Union Law," and "Factory Inspection Law" have been promulgated and implemented, with significant results. However, within the concessions, they still cannot be implemented due to the lack of understanding from the concession authorities. In addition, what Chinese workers feel most painfully is especially regarding workers within the concessions, they are not allowed to organize trade unions. The problem is most serious. Employers dismiss workers who join trade unions. Concession authorities even forcibly disband trade unions. The major strike at the Shanghai Power Company in 1933 was caused by the employer not allowing workers to organize a trade union. As a result, 54 people responsible for initiating the organization of the trade union were dismissed. This is one example. This policy violates the principles of fairness and justice. The right to assembly and association is recognized by modern democratic countries. Article 2 of the general principles in Part II of the International Labour Organization's constitution stipulates that "Workers and employers should have equal rights to assembly and association, only limited by the purpose not violating the law." Article 1 of the Chinese Trade Union Law also stipulates that "Industrial workers with 100 or more people, and professional workers with 50 or more people, may organize trade unions." The granting of this right is based on the principle of human equality. The exercise of rights does not exceed the scope permitted by law and is absolutely not restricted or infringed by any force. Chinese workers can no longer tolerate such measures by the concession authorities. We appeal to all of you at the Conference to pay close attention to the seriousness of this issue and to find a way to eliminate it. At the same time, please request the Conference to decide to recommend that the concession authorities and the governments of relevant member states change this policy as soon as possible. Otherwise, we dare not imagine the development of the future." Request the Conference to recommend that each relevant member state assist the Chinese government in prohibiting opium and potent narcotics. (Explanation) The Chinese government has shown great determination to prohibit opium and potent narcotics, such as red pills, heroin, and morphine, adopting a six-year plan to completely eradicate opium from 1935 to 1940. For drug prohibition, a two-year plan has been adopted, and extremely strict laws have been promulgated. Anyone who plants, manufactures, sells, or transports opium and narcotics will be sentenced to death. Numerous drug rehabilitation institutions have been established, enforcing compulsory detoxification. Excellent results have been achieved since its implementation. However, what China considers most difficult is that a small number of foreigners do not comply with Chinese laws and use special status or methods to transport opium and narcotics to China, such as certain nationals in North China. This behaviour violates international anti-smoking obligations and endangers friendly relations between countries. Please request the Conference to recommend that all member states earnestly caution their nationals and assist the Chinese government in preventing the occurrence of such incidents. Although this matter does not directly fall under the responsibilities of the International Labour Conference, the majority of victims are workers, and the Conference cannot sit idly by. Furthermore, regarding the issue of overseas Chinese workers smoking opium, the International Labour Office has discussed it in the report of the French labour representative, Mr. Shih Wu, and has submitted the report to this Conference, hoping that the Conference will take necessary and effective measures on this matter.

After Overcoming the Difficulties at the End of April, Silver Pawnshops Continue to Extend Loans

The Leading Investment and Support of Industry by the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, Increase of Market Chips, and Increasingly Lively Finance

Since the silver pawnshop industry in this city safely overcame the difficulties at the end of April, it now has sufficient funds to continue extending loans and rescue the market. In addition to handling rediscounts, the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications are jointly leading investment in industry. Therefore, the financial situation is quite lively. The details are recorded below:

Continuing to Extend Loans

The silver pawnshop industry in this city temporarily tightened lending during the period at the end of April to replenish reserves. Now that the difficulties have been safely overcome, and the demand for loans from various industrial and commercial sectors is quite urgent, a decision has been made to utilize the sufficient funds after the end of April to continue handling loans for various sectors. Therefore, various sectors and banks have been busy handling loan procedures in recent days. However, the number of loans is mostly small and dispersed, in order to widely rescue the market. The Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications loan committee continues to organize interbank lending.

Investing in Industry

In recent years, the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications have invested significantly in industrial loans, such as cotton yarn, flour, and chemical factories. Investment in agriculture has also reached more than 10 million yuan. Recently, commercial banks have been somewhat indifferent to industrial and commercial investment due to the impact of economic downturn. Now, a decision has been made to jointly lead investment to rescue industry, and two principles have been decided: 1. Major investments will no longer be made in investment projects already held by commercial banks to avoid conflicts. Commercial banks will continue to handle these projects themselves. 2. For projects that commercial banks are unwilling or afraid to invest in, the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications will provide loans as much as possible to maintain existing businesses and promote emerging businesses.

Lively Finance

The finance in this city is becoming increasingly lively as the silver pawnshop industry continues to handle interbank lending, indirectly rescuing various sectors. Since the bank note acceptance house has been handling interbank note acceptance, its business has developed quite well. The Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications are accepting requests from the bank note acceptance house to handle rediscounts, which is increasing the amount of liquid funds. The turnover of various sectors is more convenient, and the financial market is becoming more lively.

New Life Movement Inspection Group Dare... To Leave Shanghai for Zhejiang Today

According to reports, the impression of this trip is quite good, and the Public Security Bureau has expressed satisfaction.

Mr. Liu Xiang, the deputy head of the New Life Movement Inspection Group, went to Beijing the day before yesterday to handle important matters. Mr. Zhang Yuchong, an attache of the group, went to Hangzhou to arrange accommodation. Both have returned to Shanghai last night. They are scheduled to lead the group headquarters and the second team of inspectors this afternoon to Hangzhou for inspection and to promote the New Life Movement in Zhejiang Province. The third team of inspectors is also scheduled to depart in groups this afternoon to work in Songjiang, Jinshan, Jiashan, Haining, Jiaxing, and other counties. The first team of inspectors is also scheduled to take a sea vessel today and depart in groups to work in Ningbo, Zhenhai, Fenghua, Zhuji, Xiaoshan, and other areas. They are scheduled to return to Shanghai after a month, then travel to Jiangbei, Jinpu Railway, Longhai Railway, and other places along the line to promote the New Life Movement. According to the person in charge of the group who spoke to the National Society reporter before leaving, the group has visited various organizations, groups, schools, and factories in Shanghai since arriving last month. They are generally satisfied with the state of the New Life Movement. They acknowledge that the Public Security Bureau has been able to establish a New Life Movement section independently to promote the New Life Movement. Recently, they have also organized a female employee labour service group as an example for various agencies. Such enthusiasm for promoting the New Life Movement is rare. The Public Security Bureau is the most diligent in promoting the New Life Movement in Shanghai.

Our National Overseas Chinese Affairs Problem (Continued)

— Zhou Qigang's Radio Speech

The Form of Overseas Chinese Affairs Administration　I have already briefly discussed the definition of overseas Chinese affairs and the understanding of the problem of emigration among Chinese people. Now, I want to explain to everyone the form of our national overseas Chinese affairs administration and the key to the survival of overseas Chinese. Judging from the political history of our country, overseas Chinese affairs administration is really a newly created concept in recent times. As I said before, our country first had the fact of "people emigrating," and then the organization of overseas Chinese affairs agencies. This cause and effect is the opposite of that of other countries. In the past, our so-called overseas Chinese affairs really did not involve practical actions in administration. Because overseas Chinese affairs agencies only had a vague form in history, without specific administrative powers and functions. Looking at the historical facts of our national overseas Chinese affairs agencies, more than fifty years before the founding of the Republic of China, that is, in the first year of Xianfeng, the Qing government established Overseas Inquiry Bureaus in places such as Guangzhou, Tianjin, Xiamen, and Ningbo. At that time, it was an agency to ban and control the export of Chinese laborers. In the seventh year of the Republic of China, the Beijing government established the Overseas Labor Affairs Bureau under the State Council. In the eleventh year of the Republic of China, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau was established, and later changed to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Yuan. Its content and reality were completely empty institutions, used to restrain overseas Chinese and appease revolutionary elements, with absolutely no so-called overseas Chinese affairs policy. In the twelfth year of the Republic of China, Mr. Sun Yat-sen established the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau under the Revolutionary Government Headquarters. From the fifteenth to the seventeenth years of the Republic of China, the National Government established the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee was changed to be under the jurisdiction of the Central Party Headquarters. All these organizations were agencies to deal with the personnel issues of overseas Chinese and to promote the revolution. It was not until the twentieth year of the Republic of China that the Legislative Yuan revised the Organic Law of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee, changing the overseas Chinese affairs agency to be under the Executive Yuan of the National Government. In the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee was reorganized and established, finally forming the prototype of an overseas Chinese affairs administration agency. However, compared with the structure of overseas Chinese affairs administration agencies in other countries, it is far from satisfactory. Even compared with the overseas Chinese affairs administration organization that we actually need, there is still a long way to go. For example: 　The internal organization is not sound, with the appearance of having a large head and a small tail; 　There is a lack of systematic tools in administration. Overseas Chinese affairs bureaus in domestic ports are not yet complete, and consuls in various foreign countries still cannot directly command; 　The conditions of all overseas Chinese have not been accurately investigated and statistically analyzed, so plans for overseas Chinese affairs cannot be established; 　Overseas Chinese affairs talents have not been fully cultivated, so whenever problems arise, they are passively dealt with on an ad hoc basis, with minimal efficiency; 　The powers and responsibilities of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee and various departments are not clear. When incidents occur, various agencies adhere to established regulations and customs, lacking the spirit of cooperation. All matters are shirked and delayed, resulting in obstruction to all creation and implementation. The above are obvious manifestations of the current unsound state of overseas Chinese affairs administration. Other common mistakes include regarding overseas Chinese affairs as being encompassed by diplomacy, and even completely subsuming the implementation of overseas Chinese affairs administration under diplomacy. However, the entire realm of overseas Chinese affairs is definitely not as simple as being just a part of diplomatic problems. We must first understand that the historical facts of overseas Chinese emigration do not rely on diplomacy for development. We believe that to improve the efficiency of overseas Chinese affairs administration, the initial focus should not be on the size of the agency, but on the soundness of the organization. At the same time, the country must have a clear policy on overseas Chinese affairs. Everyone also understands that simply having an overseas Chinese affairs agency does not mean that the country has overseas Chinese affairs. It is only when there is an overseas Chinese affairs policy and the power to implement the policy that there is overseas Chinese affairs and the life of overseas Chinese affairs can be maintained. Before deciding on our overseas Chinese affairs policy, we must first clearly recognize that the rise and fall of people's emigration and the prosperity and decline of the country and nation are closely related. Otherwise, if overseas Chinese affairs are completely unrelated to national administration, and some even think that the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee is an overseas Chinese community, if such a situation continues, our national overseas Chinese affairs administration will not only be ineffective in the past decades, but also be unable to escape the state of following old ways and being perfunctory and unsound for many years to come.

The Key to the Survival of Overseas Chinese　Everyone, when we discuss the survival of overseas Chinese, we should think of the hundreds of millions of overseas Chinese scattered across the five continents. For hundreds of years, they have been able to survive to this day without the protection of national power, undoubtedly because they have special survival conditions, such as: 　Overseas Chinese are able to endure hardship and be hardworking. In various countries, the working hours have now been reduced to six to seven hours. Most of our overseas Chinese still work eight to twelve hours a day, or even longer. Year after year, except for illness, they do not stop working; 　Overseas Chinese are able to take risks and create. All the labor that Europeans and Americans are unwilling to do or dare not do, as well as the labor that local natives cannot do, our overseas Chinese can undertake with their adventurous nature and creative spirit, fighting desperately against obstacles in the natural world, dedicating their full spirit to creating careers and making contributions to the world's humanity; 　Overseas Chinese live frugally and accept low wages. Whether our overseas Chinese are workers or merchants, they all intensify their work with frugal living, adhering to the principle of benefiting others and themselves, coexisting and prospering together, adapting to local needs, without the slightest ambition, purely serving society. This is the universal fact of the survival of overseas Chinese. In addition, there are two other fundamental factors that contribute to the undiminished survival of overseas Chinese: their great peaceful character and their strong national spirit, which I must also talk about to the public. Generally speaking, for thousands of years, most of the things that humans have done in the world have contained strong plundering behaviors and tiger-like deceitful pursuits. Our overseas Chinese, based on the peaceful nature of our great nation, interact with others with humility and courtesy. As time goes on, the local people are happy to associate with them. Those so-called anti-Chinese elements are all manipulated by a small number of people who harbor evil intentions and have ulterior political motives. If we talk about ordinary natives, they certainly do not have the idea of excluding overseas Chinese. This is worth studying. Moreover, overseas Chinese have left their country for thousands of miles and resided overseas for hundreds of years, without national protection or national education and cultivation, drifting in the borders of countries with strong material civilization or in savage and backward mountainous areas. They should have been assimilated or eliminated. However, overseas Chinese are not only able to maintain the concept of the Chinese nation, but also passionately love their motherland. Therefore, foreigners call it "China with a weak country but strong people." This is the strength of the national spirit of overseas Chinese and is also the fundamental condition for the survival of overseas Chinese. Therefore, in the places where overseas Chinese are scattered overseas, we often see that their customs in life are the same as in mainland China. In overseas Chinese residences, there are often places to worship ancestors. And if it is the home of the Li family, a Chinese-style Li Mansion lantern will be hung at the entrance; if it is the Chen family, a Chen Mansion lantern will be hung. There are also Chinese-style temples built everywhere, the so-called Ya Po Temple (i.e., Guanyin) and Guan Di Temple. In the Americas, there are also so-called Chinatowns, etc. (places where overseas Chinese live mostly preserve Chinese customs). At first glance, it inevitably provokes many criticisms, saying that they are outdated and unchangeable. But if we study it deeply, overseas Chinese have always lacked national protection. If they cannot preserve the old Chinese customs, they would have long been eliminated or assimilated. Then, how can we talk about the problem of Chinese overseas affairs today? Therefore, I personally am not worried about overseas Chinese preserving old Chinese customs, but I am worried about the country not providing protection and abandoning guidance. However, if this continues, the survival conditions of overseas Chinese, as seen today, are no longer so simple. To study their future survival problems, in addition to the above-mentioned items, at a minimum, the country and society must assume considerable responsibility. Because the wheel of the times does not allow us to continue to follow old ways. Overseas Chinese are currently facing many difficulties and dangers. We must take the following rescue measures, which I would like to discuss with everyone: 1. In terms of economy, the organization of overseas Chinese themselves, whether in agriculture, industry, or commerce, must be rapidly promoted to collectivization. It should never be like the past individual independent operation. Because the former is like scattered soldiers fighting, while the latter should pay attention to group warfare. 2. The organization of overseas Chinese society used to be divided into two major parts: in the Americas, it focused on clan organizations (Chen, Li, Zhang, He, Huang, etc.); in Southeast Asia, it focused on regional organizations (such as Guangzhou, Chaozhou, Qiongya, Hakka, Fujian, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, etc.). I am not against this kind of organization, but I think it should be improved and expanded. If a clan is used as an organization, there should be no patriarchal system within it. If a region is used as an organization, there should be no tribalism. Our Premier also pointed out that it is very important to expand from the family to the nation. 3. Good customs of the past should of course be preserved, and new knowledge should also be quickly supplemented to meet the needs of the times. 4. National personnel should not be indifferent to overseas Chinese problems, or even ignore them. They should understand that the entire world problem is the problem of developing emigration. The loss of emigration is the shortening of the life of the country and the nation. 5. Improve the organization of overseas Chinese affairs administration, establish an overseas Chinese affairs policy, and cultivate overseas Chinese affairs talents. 6. Actively do our best to develop overseas Chinese education and find ways to consolidate the economic foundation of overseas Chinese. 7. Effectively implement the management of overseas Chinese emigration, such as guiding, protecting, supervising, investigating, and collecting statistics. The above is my personal superficial view on the key to the survival of overseas Chinese. Of course, our country's entire overseas Chinese affairs are more than this. But I think that in general, we must address the most urgent matters first, hoping that everyone will grasp the needs of the times on the issue of overseas Chinese affairs, catch up, and work hard. Otherwise, the future of overseas Chinese affairs will be fraught with dangers, and the vitality of the country and the nation will also be affected. (End)

Discussing Concrete Measures for Joint Resistance

The Special Zone Telephone Problem Committee believes that the Shanghai Telephone Company, regardless of the social depression, rashly implemented the new system, charging according to the number of calls, and many users have reported that the floating calculations are too high. His original letter reads, "Dear Sirs, I am one of the major shareholders of the Shanghai Telephone Company. Regarding the company's reckless price increase during this most depressed period, disregarding the difficulties of businesses, I have repeatedly sent letters of opposition, but to no avail. Those in charge lack moral values and self-respect, which is hateful and regrettable. Moreover, since I became a shareholder nearly ten years ago, the company has not distributed the official interest. The company disregards the current social situation and increases the burden on users, implementing an inhumane price increase. We do not want to increase telephone charges, but only ask for the official interest that was previously set, which is enough. Please, your association, work hard to resist and achieve final victory. I will contact the shareholders of our country who have invested in the company to be your backing, and will also rectify the internal affairs of the company, save expenses, to meet the budget and reduce the burden on users, in order to achieve the effect of cooperation. The unified public bond of 146 million yuan was issued on February 1. After the rush printing of bond certificates was completed, the bond exchange offices in this city and the Central, China, and Communications Banks in various places began handling the exchange and compensation matters on March 11. Since the deadline has not yet expired, it is still being processed. Less than one-tenth of the A and B bond certificates have not been exchanged. Yesterday, a special announcement was issued stating that the A and B bond certificates of the unified public bond are now scheduled to be drawn on the morning of May 9 at 10:00 a.m. According to a telegram from the ministry, the remaining bond certificates for exchange of the above two types should be sealed up one day before the drawing. The office is now issuing both types of bond certificates that have been exchanged, and those who have not yet received them will be issued until 3:30 p.m. on the 8th. Each of these two types of bond certificates is 15 million yuan, and the first round will repay 5/1000 of the principal, with 5 lots drawn for each, totaling 750,000 yuan in principal repayment and 4.5 million yuan in interest payment. The C and D bond certificates will be drawn in mid-June, and the E bond certificates will be drawn in mid-July. The dates have not yet been determined. The circumstances will be taken into consideration for separate cut-off and local military police will be ordered to provide protection

According to a direct telegram from the Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce on April, the ministry has already issued a telegram stating, 'This ministry, in order to show special consideration for the people in remote provinces and regions and places where legal tender is not widely circulated, who hold silver coins and silver and have not been able to exchange them for legal tender, will temporarily maintain the status quo and continue to process the exchanges. Ling Xianyang Returned to China from Europe Yesterday to Inspect Dockyard Businesses

Ling Xianyang, Deputy Manager of the Central Trust Bureau and Secretary of the Qiujiang Dockyard Construction Committee, was dispatched to Europe in January of this year to inspect dockyard businesses. He has completed his mission and returned to China via the German postal ship "Na Aishi Nu" at 1:00 p.m. yesterday. More than twenty people, including personnel from the Central Trust Bureau and relatives and friends of Ling, went to the port to welcome him. Ling told the Central News Agency reporter at the port that he left the country in the first month and visited France, Italy, Germany, Denmark, and other four countries to inspect dockyard businesses in order to learn from them. He spent four months, of which he spent the most time in France. The scope of the inspection included all issues such as passenger management, land and water intermodal transportation, and dockyard transportation equipment. Regarding his impressions of this inspection, Germany's dockyard equipment is quite complete, all using the latest machinery. Since the country's revitalization, everything has been remarkable, especially machinery, which has made special progress. Although Denmark is a small country, its dockyard business is the best in the world. The country has many dockyards, and the management and work efficiency are satisfactory in all aspects. The country has a central agency that specializes in managing dockyards and planning everything. The staff members are all serving voluntarily, planning everything in an orderly manner. Italy and France are also quite advanced, but France's handling of administrative management is slightly lacking. Labor costs in our country are low. Regarding dockyard equipment and cargo handling, machinery is certainly fast, but construction must also be determined according to the needs of the environment. He will compile an inspection report and submit it to President Kong and the Qiujiang Dockyard Construction Committee for reference.

County Government Announcement Strict Pursuit of Tax Arrears from 1935

Orders Each District to Be Responsible for Collection and Payment

The Shanghai County Government issued an announcement yesterday stating that the unpaid strings outside the county limit have always been collected and paid by each district to the treasury, and the amount has been cleared year by year. Now, according to the order of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, the interception of strings for collection is prohibited in order to avoid abuses. However, the district system in the county has been in place for a long time and the results are obvious. We should understand the decree, adapt to local conditions, and make changes as appropriate. All tax arrears from 1935 will be collected and paid by each district to the treasury, recognizing and copying the names of the defaulting households under their jurisdiction and the amount due. If there are households who arbitrarily refuse to pay, the district is allowed to report the names to the collection official and submit them to the government for strict pursuit in accordance with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's salt tax Ganzhou telegram method. In addition to instructing each district to comply, this announcement is hereby issued so that the public is aware of it. This announcement is issued by Ye Zhendong, the County Magistrate.

Ministry of Finance Responds to Chamber of Commerce Regarding Doubtful Stamp Tax on Remittance Receipts

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously reported that the Jiangsu Provincial Farmer's Bank in Shengze remitted two copies each of the original and duplicate receipts, each with a face value of 30 cents of national currency. The original receipt was printed with the phrase "Stamp Tax of 2 cents to be affixed by the recipient." The Chamber of Commerce, believing that receipts with a face value of less than three yuan were not required to be stamped according to the law, sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance requesting clarification. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance issued a reply with document number Shui Zi 9399, stating: "The telegram and copies of the remittance receipts have been received. Remittance receipts are considered as receipts for money and differ from drafts. If the remittance amount received is three yuan or more, the recipient should affix a stamp to the original receipt in accordance with the law. The duplicate receipt is a copy and is exempt from stamping. The Jiangsu Provincial Farmer's Bank's belief that all such receipts, regardless of the amount, must be stamped with a 2-cent stamp is a misunderstanding. You are hereby notified. The original and duplicate receipts (four copies) are returned herewith for your perusal."

Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief General Association Sends Representatives to Report on Work to Overseas Chinese

The Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief General Association, located at 505 Henan Road, is a charitable organization jointly formed by enthusiastic Chinese and foreign philanthropists. Since advocating construction for disaster relief, its scope has expanded daily, its work has gradually progressed, and its achievements have been outstanding, rarely matched. It has been repeatedly praised by society and rewarded by the government. Overseas Chinese compatriots also have great faith in it, and the number of those who voluntarily remit funds to assist has been increasing daily. Last year, during the fundraising for flood relief, donations from overseas Chinese accounted for nearly half of the total, demonstrating their strong support. The association believes that because overseas Chinese are far away and communication is limited, they may not be fully aware of all the work done over the years. Therefore, it is taking the opportunity of Mr. Baker, the current consultant to the Central Trust Bureau of the Ministry of Finance and executive member of the association, returning to his country on leave, and Mr. Luo Chuanhua, the director of the Shanghai office, being selected to attend the Pacific International Studies Conference in the United States, to request both gentlemen to report in detail on the domestic disaster situation and the projects being undertaken to overseas Chinese compatriots in various cities in Japan, Canada, Honolulu, and major cities in the United States, and to solicit suggestions. It is reported that Mr. Baker is scheduled to depart first on the 19th of this month, and Mr. Luo will depart next month.

Judge's Advice Leads to Reconciliation, Husband and Wife as Before

Reunion After Separation, Compassionate Advice, Shao Di Realizes and Returns Home with Husband

Xu Xiaomei, a local young woman residing at No. 7 Yongxin Lane, Daxilu, West Shanghai, is 22 years old this year. In 1931, at the age of 18, she married Xu Xueshan (about the same age as the woman) with Zhu Wenqing and Li Liuquan as matchmakers. After the marriage, the couple's affection grew deeper, but the good times did not last long. After three months, Xu's behavior changed, and he sought new love outside, neglecting and frequently abusing Xiaomei. On June 1st of the lunar calendar last year, the couple argued over trivial matters, and Xiaomei, unable to bear the constant beatings, fled to the Mengjiangtang Nunnery in Yuji Bridge, intending to have her hair cut and become a nun. After being dissuaded by the abbess, she was greeted home by relatives of both sides. However, Xu Xueshan remained unrepentant and forced Xiaomei back to her mother's home in a few days. Recently, Xu Xiaomei, feeling that her husband was so unfaithful and it was impossible to grow old together, filed a petition with the Civil Mediation Office of the Second Special District Court, requesting mediation for divorce, and requesting an order for the defendant Xu Xueshan to pay living expenses of 30 yuan per month until the age of 60, totaling 15,480 yuan. The court granted the request, and yesterday morning, Judge Guo Huaipu summoned both parties to court for mediation. First, the petitioner Xu Xiaomei stated the purpose of her request for mediation, and the defendant Xu Xueshan opposed the divorce and was willing to welcome his wife home to live with him. After the court advised them on the pain of separation and reunion, the petitioner suddenly no longer wanted a divorce and was willing to go home to live together. At this point, the court announced that the mediation was successful. After Xu and his wife left the court, they left together.

Police Crack Down on Forgery of Consular Seals from Various Countries, Strict Investigation Due to Suspected Political Implications, Two Russians and One Chinese Detained Pending Further Trial

At around 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, a Russian named Ai Like Changte Jia Chai Qingge, residing at the Salvation Army Hostel on Xiamen Road (formerly the Western Prison), reported to the Old Gate Police Station that a signature book used when he traveled around various countries had been stolen and requested an investigation. The Chief of the Mountain Police ordered Western Detective Su Haofu and Chinese Detective He Renrui to investigate. While the detectives were preparing to accompany Ai to his residence for investigation, Ai suddenly left the police station, his whereabouts unknown. The Chinese and Western detectives then went to the reported residence. Upon arriving at the open space of the Salvation Army Hostel, they saw Ai holding a paper package. Suspecting him, they went up and asked why he had left the police station without permission. When Ai saw the detectives, he hid the paper package inside his clothes. Suspecting him, the detectives took the package and opened it. Inside were forged consular seals from various countries, such as the seals of the Philippine French Consulate, the Manila French Consulate, and the Chinese Consulate in Iloilo, as well as letters. They also found a bottle of ink eraser in Ai's room and brought it back to the police station along with the seals. Suspecting political implications, they notified the Municipal Public Security Bureau, the French Concession Police Department Political Section, and the Public Concession Police Department Political Section. Each sent personnel to the Old Gate Police Station for joint interrogation. According to Ai's confession, he was preparing to forge a passport because he intended to leave China. The two seals of the Philippine and Manila French Consulates were purchased from Chi Rigan, a Cantonese residing at No. 3, Alley 272, Wuchang Road, Beiyihe China Shipping Club, for eight yuan. The detectives then went to the club to arrest Chi, but he was not there. They found several seals of the Finnish, Polish, and Egyptian Consulates, as well as letters, in his room. Later, Chinese Detective He Renrui arrested him at the Dadong Hotel. In addition to the name Chi Rigan, Chi also used the names Xi Qiangsheng, Yimanuoer Aiduohua, and Feilankai Tuo. A further search of Room 4 of the Wusong Hotel at No. 616, Wusong Road, resulted in the arrest of another accomplice, a Russian named Fula Dimao Kaier Tuo. Chi Rigan claimed at the police station that he was British. The Chief of Police ordered Western Detective Smith to investigate at the British Consulate, but the British Consulate did not recognize him. Therefore, yesterday morning, the three suspects were escorted to the First Special District Court Criminal Division 1. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the circumstances, stating that the actions of the defendants had unknown motives and were still under investigation. Therefore, he requested detention in accordance with Articles 76 and 101 of the Criminal Procedure Law and submitted the seized evidence. Judge Feng Shide reviewed the report and ordered that the three suspects Ai and others be detained for one week.

Desperate Thief Swallows Gold Ring

Sentenced to Ten Months After Interrogation

Zhou Achun, a thief from Nanjing, 26 years old, specialized in robbing women of their gold rings, wallets, and purses on the streets of the French Concession. At 6:00 PM on the 30th of last month, an elderly woman from Suzhou, Zhu Jinyu, 61 years old, residing at No. 16 Yili, Jialele Road, took a rickshaw from her home for some errands. When passing the back door of the Slaughterhouse at the intersection of Geluokelu and Huanghe Road, Zhou saw that the old woman was old and easily deceived. He caught up from behind and snatched a gold ring worth three yuan. He fled along Pishaonai Road towards the intersection of Dongmintiniluyin Road. The old woman shouted "Catch the thief!" The patrol police saw it and helped chase and capture Zhou. Zhou, in desperation, put the stolen goods in his mouth and swallowed it. After being arrested, he swallowed it and was unable to search. He was taken to the police station and first sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Yesterday, the police sent Zhou to the Criminal Division 1 of the Second Special District Court. Judge Wang Gangxu interrogated him. The Legal Department lawyer Fei Xizhen explained the case and prosecuted him for robbery. Then, the victim, Zhu Yu, explained the situation of the robbery. When Zhou Achun was interrogated, he said, "I came to Shanghai to borrow money from my old boss, who promised to give it to me on the 28th of last month. However, I was unable to borrow it, which led me to become homeless in Shanghai. I was impoverished and had no way to rob to make money to go home." The court reviewed the confession, announced the conclusion of the debate, and sentenced Zhou Achun to ten months of imprisonment for robbery.

The matter was discovered by Xing Wenzhu, a fellow villager and friend of Fei, who secretly told Wu to check under the cabinet. There were indeed two packages of red pills, one wrapped in yellow cloth and one wrapped in black cloth. The next day, Xing came again and said that Fei had found out that he had exposed his plot and was making things difficult for him. As Xing was about to leave the alley with the money, detectives Ni and Zhang stepped forward, arrested him, and searched him for the legal tender. Afterwards, they went to No. 318 Yangzho Road, arrested Fei and Tao, and took them to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court. The three defendants were questioned, and their confessions were ambiguous. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered them to be remanded and re-examined after the investigation.

Zhu Xiongwu and Others Accused of Defamation, High Court President's Case Transferred to Shanghai for Trial, He Jinshi and Chen Shitao Promoted to Prosecute Zhu Xiongwu and Others, Requested Transfer of Jurisdiction After Public Prosecution

Zhu Xiongwu, former clerk of the Jiangsu High Court, is from Yiwu County, Zhejiang Province. He is the nephew of Zhu Xianwen, former President of the Jiangsu High Court and Counselor of the Ministry of Judicial Administration. Zhu Xiongwu has been working in the High Court for more than ten years and has been the chief clerk of the First Civil Division. In the winter of 1935, Zhu Xiongwu's reputation was poor, and he was reported to the Ministry of Justice by the current President of the High Court, Zhu Shusheng, and ordered to be dismissed. Unexpectedly, Zhu and a group of colleagues who had also been dismissed printed leaflets in the name of the Jiangsu Judicial Improvement Association, defaming President Zhu. They were acting as witnesses for the divisional clerks in office. After Zhu Xiongwu was dismissed, he probed the results of a certain property division case, which was also listed in the leaflet. Therefore, President Zhu ordered Prosecutor Lu Wenqin of the Wu County Local Court to search Zhu Xiongwu's Suzhou residence. Although the leaflets were not found, letters between Zhu and Shanghai lawyer He Yi regarding the case of Miao Wen's obstruction of national currency were found, so Zhu Xiongwu was detained. It was later found that Zhu Xiongwu and lawyer Shu Feilu Wenguang were smoking opium together, so the Lu's house was searched, and evidence of fraud and a book of cases handled were found, so Lu was also detained. Zhu Xiongwu was also sent to the Anti-Smoking Committee for punishment for smoking opium. In the midst of the uproar, Chen Chaozuan (from the same town as Zhu), who had previously served as a clerk in the High Court, had been ordered to transfer to the First Branch of the Xiaojiang Oil High Court last year. Unexpectedly, his wife saw Zhu Xiongwu's arrest in Suzhou and wrote a letter to her husband in Qingjiangpu, saying that all the evidence had been hidden, etc., which was discovered by the president of the court. Chen Chaozuan and Zhu Xiongwu were suspected of jointly defaming President Zhu, and Chen was handed over to the Prosecutor's Office and escorted to Suzhou. He was also detained by the Wu County Local Court, and his hands were searched. At the same time, the prosecutor repeatedly summoned witnesses for interrogation. Therefore, Shanghai lawyer He Qi was asked by the Wu County Local Court to assist in the arrest and escort to Suzhou, and the promotion of Chen Shitao, a judge of the Wuxi Local Court, was guaranteed. Until recently, He Qi was first found not guilty due to lack of evidence, and Judge Chen Qitao dismissed the prosecution. Zhu Xiongwu, Lu Wenguang, Chen Chaozuan, and Chen's wife were all publicly prosecuted. However, most of the defendants were former High Court officials, and the President of the High Court was the victim in this case. Therefore, it was considered that there was a risk of bias in the trial in the same place, so they applied for a transfer of jurisdiction. The application has been approved by the higher court, and the case has been transferred to the Shanghai Court for trial.

A new house at No. 172, Chunyang Lane, No. 211 Dongyouheng Road, is currently unoccupied. On the afternoon of the 5th of this month, at around 1 PM, Zheng Hongmao Glass Store at No. 383 Wusong Road sent an apprentice, Zhong Zhishan (age 18, from Chongming), to fit a piece of glass in the front building. The apprentice fell out of the window, suffering a severe head injury. A painter working downstairs saw this and immediately reported it to the Jiaxing Road police station. An ambulance was called to the scene, and he was rushed to Tongren Hospital. However, the treatment was ineffective, and he died at 11:30 AM the day before yesterday. The police station sent detective Gu Wenyao to investigate. The body was then taken to the forensic examination office on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, Zhang Zongru, a prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Court, arrived at the office to examine the body. First, Chief Chinese Constable Li Jingshou reported the previous situation. Then, Zheng Bolin testified that he was the owner of the glass store. The deceased had been learning this trade in another store for more than two years and had only been at his place for fifty days. He was introduced by his third older brother, who is not currently in Shanghai, so the deceased's family could not be notified. He requested to temporarily claim the body. After hearing the testimony, Zhang ruled that Zhong Zhishan, male, had died from a head injury caused by a work-related fall. The body was handed over to his shop owner, Zheng Bolin, for claiming and burial.

Rickshaw Licenses Extended to Tomorrow

Regarding the dispute between rickshaw merchants and the Municipal Council, according to news from the Vehicle Committee of the Municipal Council, the rickshaw merchants have recently paid all of the May license fees to the Municipal Council. At the same time, the bank receipts for the April Mutual Aid Society fees have also been submitted to the Municipal Council, and a written guarantee has been made to pay the Mutual Aid Society fees for this month by the end of this month. However, to obtain rickshaw licenses, each rickshaw owner must bring their owner's certificate for endorsement. Since the owner's certificates have been jointly stored in the bank by the rickshaw owners, it is temporarily difficult to issue so many rickshaw licenses. Request to Fill in the French Concession Canal

Residents Recently Submitted Letters to the Health Bureau

Residents of western Shanghai, including Zhu Bofan, in view of the existence of the French Concession Canal, which is not only useless but also hinders public health and international image, have written to the Municipal Health Bureau, requesting that it jointly work with the Public Works Bureau to fill it in as soon as possible. The letter states: "The original French Concession Canal in western Shanghai, starting from Xujiahui in the south, passes through various polluted areas. The river water is completely black. Every summer, the stench not only reaches the gate of Datong University but also extends to Daxilu. The river has long been silted up and blocked, and the mosquitoes and flies produced here are extremely fierce. They fly everywhere, whether day or night, and are not afraid of people at all. Therefore, the Chinese and foreign residents nearby are all complaining and expressing dissatisfaction. The location of the canal connects the junction of the Chinese and French Concessions. At a time when this new movement is being promoted, leaving such an unclean stain in Shanghai is detrimental to public health and damages the international image. Therefore, we hereby submit a letter requesting your esteemed bureau to quickly send staff to investigate and, together with the Public Works Bureau, immediately carry out the filling in of the canal to show the practical implementation of the principles of promoting a new life." Apart from rickshaw business representatives Yin Zhiling and Hou Shaocan, who were absent, all other directors attended the meeting on time. The most important matters discussed were the reports of the various committees. According to the report of the Insurance Committee, rickshaw puller insurance was officially established on May 1st. After the death of a member, his family can receive compensation of 40 yuan in national currency. There are also specific compensation amounts for those who lose limbs or eyesight due to accidents. Furthermore, the Medical Committee reported that the Western District Branch Hospital is insufficient and that all beds have been decided to increase from eighteen to twenty-six. The hospital's medical services are extremely busy, and it has various benefits that it is run by the Mutual Aid Society itself. However, patients who cannot be accommodated by the hospital still need to be sent to other hospitals, and their expenses will be compensated.

The Personnel Committee held a meeting on February 29th and made the following decisions: Actively seek a cemetery address for rickshaw pullers in northern Shanghai; Contact preferential prices for coffins and notify rickshaw pullers' families; Lower-level staff of the Mutual Aid Society should be able to join the insurance plan; Add a primary school for rickshaw pullers' children on Robberon Road, but before that, a survey should be conducted on the number of rickshaw pullers' children living in the area; Establish a rickshaw pullers' savings bank.

The above reports of the various committees, as well as the society's periodic financial reports and the situation of relief work, have all been passed by the board of directors. According to a recent report, a total of 30 rickshaw puller representatives from five districts submitted a report to the society before the board meeting, stating that all 28,564 rickshaw pullers in the Shanghai Public Concession have signed a printed petition, listing the registration number, name, and fingerprints of each rickshaw puller, and submitted it to the chief of the Municipal Council, clearly acknowledging that the Mutual Aid Society fees are specifically used for the welfare undertakings of all registered rickshaw pullers, declaring that they are very willing to continue to pay. The 30 rickshaw puller representatives certified that there was no fabrication or duplication in these petitions. The rickshaw license office also verified that there were no errors in the names, numbers, and fingerprints of the rickshaw pullers. It was found that this type of petition was spontaneously organized by the rickshaw pullers because the rickshaw owners resolutely declared that the rickshaw pullers were unwilling to continue paying the Mutual Aid Society fees to express the true intentions of the rickshaw pullers. The rickshaw pullers who have signed have reached 80% of the total number of registered rickshaw pullers and were obtained in one day, which also shows the inaccuracy of the rickshaw owners' counter-propaganda. Furthermore, the revised constitution and by-laws of the Mutual Aid Society, in Chinese and English, have now been printed. Those interested in this matter can request to read them nearby. The Mutual Aid Society's report, up to the end of 1935, has been published in Chinese, while the English version is still in print.

In Jinling

— Sightseeing Tour of the New Destiny - Bai Liu

Smoke veils the cold water, the moon illuminates the sandy shores, moored at night by the Qinhuai River near a tavern:

The merchant girls are oblivious to the sorrows of a fallen nation, across the river they incessantly sing "The Flowers of the Rear Courtyard."

The sixty-li-long, expansive Stone City, once possessed a glorious history! The lingering aura of the Six Dynasties once made this land shine! Imagine, when it was the capital of emperors in the past, those who dwelled here were undoubtedly all elegantly dressed figures! As it was the center of culture and politics, romance and darkness were also contained and flourishing within it. On the Qinhuai River, painted boats came and went. The taverns on both banks resounded with music and songs throughout the night. Mad indulgence. It's just like a young woman forgetting herself when favored!

However, she has aged. Now she is an aging noblewoman, she has been forgotten. Now she is once again brought up from oblivion, but the smile on that aged face cannot conceal the mottled traces of tears!

The sixty-li-long city wall, bearing wounds, silently, for hundreds of years, remains the same.

The Qinhuai River, like the belt of an abandoned noblewoman, still faithfully surrounds Jinling!

Those densely packed houses, however, have witnessed countless changes in people's lives; they have seen a lively soul emerge and disappear without a trace, until the appearance of the next batch. They have witnessed the vicissitudes of fate of generations of descendants.

Now, the pampered and weak descendants are struggling in the wind and rain day and night.

"Can they struggle through?"

"Can they truly wash away all the tears and restore that proud countenance?"

Originally, due to its geographical environment and the determination of its historical destiny, this society has always been progressing. While other parts were still lingering in the medieval rural social stage, this place was about to leap into an industrial and commercial social form. However, in its development path, it encountered obstruction and destruction!

The peaceful days gradually had disturbances, and finally the torrent rushed in, causing turbulence and looting of this comfortable society!

The seedlings of industry were broken and oppressed, and could only develop morbidly towards the path of commerce. All national capital turned into the process of comprador of imperialists, or invaded the countryside, concentrated land rights, and deprived the peasants of their happiness. If this contradiction is not resolved, society will develop even more morbidly! The shadows of society will fill the entire society even more.

Because this society's development has undergone changes, its progress is very slow. After so many days, the difference in progress in between is very limited. The hierarchical structure of this society has also changed very little. Therefore, the division of its social classes still shows the form of a rural society. The opposition between classes is not as strict and distant as in an industrial society!

Generally speaking, the social classes here are: the upper class is the aristocracy, landlords, large merchants, and a small number of industrialists. The next class is the middle-class merchants, independent farmers, handicraftsmen, and general freelancers. The next layer is small merchants, tenant farmers, and general morbid products such as singing girls and prostitutes. The bottom layer is poor farmers, workers, apprentices, and general social parasites.

Although it is said that society has divided into classes following natural trends, are these classes permanently fixed? Are they permanently isolated from each other? A new, great force is attempting to control natural trends and remove the layers of shadows from society under the broad daylight! In Jinling, the sudden appearance of one or two miracles foreshadows the movement of shadows. A ray of light shines far away on the horizon.

The capital city is indeed the political center at present, but it does not contain any corruption. All civil servants have been infected by a new spirit. They have mostly become or are becoming people of a new era. There is no corruption contained within this! Most recently, following civilian training, civil servants also undergo training. At dawn or dusk, one can often see many white-bearded civil servants standing in formation "one two one."

There are many soldiers wearing military uniforms and horizontal or diagonal leather belts, especially on Sundays, almost every alley has their shadows. They are all modern soldiers, modern Chinese soldiers. People say that the era can be reflected in thought and literature, I say that it can also be reflected in the spirit of soldiers. In the era of warlord separatism, there were those wolfish and fierce soldiers; and in this era when the depression has reached its extreme and society is about to turn over, a new force will inevitably emerge. This force is contained in a group of new soldiers. They all have pure hearts, lofty thoughts and humble attitudes. On buses, they often give up their seats, and they often enthusiastically engage in public welfare undertakings. They have a spirit of practical work.

These, these are all harbingers of social turnaround! The shadows of society are moving, and a ray of light is shining far away on the horizon.

However, due to the existence of contradictions in the times, the shadows of society are very thick.

On cold, windy days, batches of people in tattered clothes, old and young, huddle in the streets and alleys, emitting miserable wails. Thousands of people gather at the gates of porridge kitchens to beg for food.

Many rough-handed and coarse-footed girls have been added to the banks of the Qinhuai River. In the employment agencies, many pitiful eyes are looking forward to something.

The population of the capital city increases every year, affecting the expansion of the lower layers of society. These people all come from the countryside. It can be seen that rural bankruptcy is serious! For example, in the Jiangbei area, year after year, due to the harm of floods and droughts and the invasion of commercial capital, the land of general small and medium-sized farmers has been exploited. This has made them unable to stand firm in the countryside, so they have to come to the city to find their destiny. The old and weak can only beg for food. Men, if they are lucky, can find some work. If they are unlucky, they are forced by livelihood and can only become bandits. Young women enter employment agencies, and young girls can only sell themselves into prostitution.

Furthermore, as the capital city is the political center, generally unemployed intellectuals come here to find a way out. If you go to a small inn run by local people in this city, you will see many sallow-faced young people lying on thin bedding, eating sesame cakes and spending their days in year-like despair! Every day you can also read the cries of unemployed young people in the newspapers.

Making the rural farmers touch their mottled backs and shed tears, the slums are always cold, orphaned and helpless children sell things on the streets day and night, more than four thousand banner people recall their past power and are in a daze, and the shantytowns are often full of curses of fate, these are even more needless to say!

However, these are precisely the products of the contradictions of the times. To adjust them, unless we fundamentally resolve the contradictions of this era!

We must destroy all forces that restrict our development of vitality! We must remove all external sinister and oppressive forces, otherwise, the development of vitality will be restricted, and social diseases will continue to arise! The whole society only hears cries and wails!

Although Jinling is dressed in new clothes, the broad Zhongshan Road, tall buildings and mansions, and majestic government agencies, can't hide that lonely face and mottled traces of tears!

The Ming Mausoleum silently watches, and the Zhongshan Mausoleum also gazes from afar on Zhongshan Mountain! (The End)
