Education News

Regulations for Establishing Free and Publicly Funded School Places at All Levels of Schools

The Ministry of Education Orders All Schools, Bureaus, and Departments to Implement Starting Next Semester

(Nanjing, 7th) The Ministry of Education, based on the principles of the "Methods for Establishing Free and Publicly Funded School Places at All Levels of Schools" approved by the Executive Yuan, has formulated the relevant regulations and issued an order on the 7th to all public and private colleges and universities, and to all school bureaus and departments, to strictly comply starting next academic year. From now on, children with outstanding talents or young people with excellent academic performance and conduct, even if their families are poor, can expect to have an equal opportunity to receive a complete education due to the preferential treatment of the country and society. The full text of the regulations, consisting of twenty articles, outlines the main points as follows: In order to reward and assist students from poor families who are physically sound, have outstanding talents, and achieve excellent results, schools should establish free and publicly funded school places in accordance with the provisions of the regulations. Free school places shall be exempt from tuition fees, as well as physical education, library, experimental and other similar fees. Private schools should, in accordance with the following provisions, collect small amounts in special circumstances. Primary schools should set up free school places for more than 40% of the total number of children in the school. At least 20% should be set up in the 25th year, and then gradually increased year by year, with the limit to reach the standard of 40% in the 28th year. (B) Secondary schools, junior and senior high schools, and junior and senior vocational schools, should set up free school places for more than 15% of the total number of students in the school. At least 8% should be set up in the 25th year, and then gradually increased year by year, with the limit to reach the standard of 15% in the 28th year. (C) Colleges and universities should set up free school places for more than 10% of the total number of students in the school. At least 5% should be set up in the 25th year, and then gradually increased year by year, with the limit to reach the standard of 10% in the 28th year. In addition to being exempt from tuition fees, publicly funded school places should also be given the minimum food, lodging, uniforms, books, and other expenses in accordance with the provisions of Article 16. All levels of public schools across the country, in addition to setting up free school places, should also set up publicly funded school places in accordance with the following provisions: (A) Ordinary primary schools and short-term primary schools should set up at least 4% of the total number of students in the 25th year, and then gradually increase the number. (B) Vocational schools, junior and senior high schools, and junior and senior vocational schools, should set up at least 3% of the total number of students in the 25th year, and then gradually increase the number. The publicly funded treatment of secondary normal schools shall be handled in accordance with the regulations for normal schools. (C) Colleges and universities should set up at least 2% of the total number of students in the 25th year, and then gradually increase the number. Private schools at all levels with relatively sufficient funding or receiving government assistance should also consider setting up publicly funded school places. The funding for setting up publicly funded school places in public schools at all levels across the country should be based on the principle of reducing expenditures within the school's regular expenses. Before the start of each summer vacation, schools at all levels should determine the number of free and publicly funded school places to be set up in the next year based on the general number of students in each approved school and the proportion specified in these regulations, and report it to the competent education administrative authorities. At the end of each academic year, schools at all levels should report the free and publicly funded school places that have been set up in the current year, as well as the list of free and publicly funded students, to the competent education administrative authorities. The free and publicly funded school places that should be set up by schools at all levels should be allocated to students in each grade of the school. The number of places allocated to newly recruited students in the following year should also be included in the admission brochure for public announcement. Students from poor families whose families are unable to afford the cost of their children's schooling may seek two or more reliable guarantors to apply for proof from the competent education administrative authorities in their original county or city, or in the county or city where they have resided for more than three years. The competent education administrative authorities in each county and city should organize a review committee for free and publicly funded school places to review the aforementioned applications. Those who are qualified shall be submitted to the county mayor or city mayor for the issuance of a certificate of poverty. Before the establishment of the review committee, the aforementioned review and certification may be temporarily handled by the county or city education administrative authorities under the authority of the county mayor or city mayor. Those who apply for free or publicly funded treatment should do so in accordance with the following provisions: (A) Applicants should submit a certificate of poverty at the time of registration. (B) Students in school should submit a certificate of poverty before the start of each academic year. Schools at all levels that set up both free school places and publicly funded school places in accordance with these regulations should give the publicly funded school places to students from poor families whose entrance examination results or school grades are better. For students who receive free or publicly funded treatment, if their conduct and academic performance average less than Grade B, the schools may stop their free or publicly funded treatment. Schools should organize a committee to jointly review and approve the granting of free and publicly funded school places. Schools that set up publicly funded school places shall determine the expenses given to students within the following ranges according to the local living conditions: ordinary primary schools, 10 to 30 yuan per person per year; junior high schools and junior vocational schools, 40 to 80 yuan per person per year; senior high schools and senior vocational schools, 60 to 100 yuan per person per year; colleges and universities, 150 to 150 yuan per person per year. The treatment of publicly funded school places in short-term primary schools shall be determined by each school according to the local situation. If students who have graduated from free and publicly funded schools are found to have falsely claimed poverty or forged certificates, the schools may recover all fees from the student or their guarantor after verification, and may stop issuing academic transcripts or graduation certificates. Within two months after the start of each academic year, the education bureaus of each province and city, and public and private colleges and universities, should report the progress of handling free and publicly funded quotas to the Ministry of Education for record-keeping. Various scholarships and quotas established by schools, the funding for which comes from public or private institutions, organizations, or individuals, and is not paid from the school's regular budget, should still be maintained and should not be used to offset the free or publicly funded quotas stipulated in these regulations.

City Education Bureau Announcement

The Preliminary Examination for Relief of Graduates from Unregistered Private High Schools in This City to Enter Higher Education Will Be Held in Mid-June

The Registration Period is from June 1st to 10th

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau announced that it had received many requests from graduates of unregistered private high schools regarding their qualifications and seeking relief. Hired Mr. Bingnan to be responsible for Western newspaper publicity matters; Selected excellent exhibits to print postcards for the audience to purchase, to be handled jointly by the General Affairs and Evaluation Divisions; Approved the guidelines for visitors, the drafting and production of slogans to be handled jointly by the General Affairs and Compilation Divisions; Standing committee members should take turns being stationed at the venue during the exhibition period, and Hu Shuyi was appointed as the venue director, Deng Yi as the general traffic commander, and Yuan Zengyu as the general order commander; The General Affairs Division shall formulate the method for selling items at the venue; Sent a letter to the Public Utilities Bureau requesting them to instruct various transportation companies to give children half-price fares and increase the number of vehicles during the exhibition period; Each committee member should submit a special article by May 20 for publication in the journal; The exhibit labels should be remade for uniformity, to be handled jointly by the Compilation and Evaluation Divisions; Approved the content of the venue guidebook; Appointed Fu Boliang as the deputy director of the Exhibition Division; The method of decorating the exhibits was handed over to the Exhibition, Evaluation, and General Affairs Divisions for planning; Approved the methods for evaluating and awarding children's painting performances and exhibits; Requested art supply manufacturers to donate materials for children's painting performances, to be handled by the General Affairs Division; Recognized the additional appointments of division secretaries; Staff members of this committee who have other positions shall be granted official leave by their original work units without deducting salary; Telegraphed the National Children's Art Implementation Association to forward a telegram to the Ministry of Education and to various provinces, cities, and districts to send exhibits immediately; Scheduled a discussion meeting for the evaluation committee members; Produced badges for the committee staff, to be designed by Guo Kechang.

Guidelines for Visitors: Group visitors should have the leader fill in the number of visitors and the name of the group on the signature book; Individual visitors must sign in first; Visitors must move forward in order and must not rush ahead; Visitors must walk on the left side; Visitors must not talk or laugh loudly in the venue; Visitors must move forward according to the prescribed route and must not retreat; Visitors must not smoke in the venue; Visitors must not spit arbitrarily in the venue; Visitors must walk lightly in the venue; Visitors must not point with their fingers when viewing paintings; Visitors must not discard paper scraps or fruit peels in the venue; Visitors may go to the information desk or ask the on-site reception staff if they have any questions; Visitors must abide by the guidelines for visitors.

Evaluation Method: The exhibits of this exhibition will be evaluated according to the exhibit evaluation standards; The exhibits will first be divided into groups for evaluation according to the exhibit catalog, with a total of eight groups. Each group will be freely determined by the evaluation committee members, but each group must have at least three or more members; An evaluation form will be prepared for group evaluation. Each work must be filled out with one form, and one member will be elected from each group to be responsible for recording; After the group evaluation is completed, all evaluation committee members will conduct a joint evaluation based on the group evaluation results; At the end of the evaluation, each evaluation committee member will submit a report separately, and several members will be elected to organize it.

The Vocational Education Society Decides to Raise Funds to Purchase an Airplane to Celebrate Chiang Kai-shek's Birthday

Fundraising will commence from the 11th of this month and will be limited to one month. All collected funds will be sent together.

The Chinese Vocational Education Society recently received a letter from the General Association of the China Aviation Association, along with the "Methods for Expanding the Aviation Patriotic Movement in Shanghai City and Raising Funds to Purchase an Airplane to Celebrate Chiang Kai-shek's Birthday." The Society believes that self-improvement and national humiliation evoke universal sympathy, and that saving the nation and ensuring its survival are matters of inescapable duty. Now that the central government authorities are exhausting their wisdom and loyalty in shouldering the great responsibility of saving the nation, all citizens should do their best according to their abilities and contribute to the purchase of an airplane to celebrate Chiang Kai-shek's birthday and strengthen national defense. There is no better way to serve the country. Therefore, starting from May 11th, the Society will earnestly discuss and encourage each other, and all colleagues in the offices and affiliated institutions, as well as students and farmers, will donate whatever amount they can afford to purchase the airplane. The donations will be purely voluntary, without any compulsion. The general affairs section of the office, and the heads of the one, two, and three supplementary schools, and the chief instructor in the suburbs of Shanghai, will be responsible for collecting and forwarding the funds. The names of all donors, regardless of the amount donated, will be disclosed in the Guoxun Weekly. The fundraising will be completed within one month.

Nanjing Huwen Girls' High School Academic Exhibition

Nanjing Huwen Girls' High School was founded in the 25th year before the Republic of China by Miss Shadnna of the American Methodist Church. It initially had only six students. Since 1927, when Madam Liu Fen, the wife of the late educator and former Southeast University President Dr. Liu Boming, became the headmistress, the school's reputation has grown daily and its achievements have been remarkable. The student body has now increased to seven high school classes and nine junior high school classes, totaling more than 600 students. The school's annual expenditure is more than 60,000 yuan, with the church providing a subsidy of less than 10,000 yuan. The remaining expenses are managed and maintained by the headmistress through administrative income planning. Two years ago, the Nanjing Municipal Social Bureau awarded the school a bonus for its excellent exam results. In the past two years, the school has consistently ranked among the top performers in competitions such as cleanliness, winning the overall championship at the city sports meet, first place in Mandarin speech contests, air defense lectures, Boy Scout drills and camping, and general cleanliness inspections. Headmistress Liu Fen treats the school as her home and the students as her children. The school motto is "Sincerity, Perseverance, Diligence, and Simplicity," and moral education emphasizes character transformation. She maintains frequent contact with students' families, holding parent-teacher conferences and visiting parents to discuss matters related to cooperation in education. In order to give students' families a clearer understanding of the school's internal affairs, the school is showcasing students' academic achievements in various subjects such as civics, science, literature, history, crafts, and art, regardless of their grades, in an open exhibition on May 4th and 5th. Over 8,000 people visited the exhibition in those two days. General comments praised the school's Chinese language achievements, such as diaries and essays, as being well-corrected. Students' calligraphy was also excellent. History and geography displays, particularly those related to national humiliation, were thought-provoking and helpful in arousing national rejuvenation. The school's administrative exhibition featured organizational charts, statistical tables, and various statistics, all clearly presented. The artwork was also precise. In particular, the achievements in science best reflected the rapid progress made in the past two years, due to the school's improved experimental facilities and the collaborative efforts of teachers and students.

Five schools participated in the meet: Yancheng, Jinling, Dehan, Qingxin, and Shanghai University. Commercial News

Finance The Bullish Situation Collapses The Gold Market Feels More and More Unsupported

Initially Concealed, Then Weak, and Then Dropped Two Yuan One The Lowest Price One Thousand One Hundred and Thirty-Three Yuan and a Half Forty-One Bull and Bear Heads Counted Together

The buying in the gold market was still weak yesterday. The bullish side has now shown signs of collapse. Therefore, although the central bank came to open cash, it was difficult to curb the real air. It once fell to a low price of one thousand one hundred and thirty-three yuan and a half. At the beginning of the morning, overseas silver markets showed English shrinkage and American stability, and the forward price of Jaderi fell by five hao to one li. Exchange rates all showed signs of contraction. The price of raw gold in London rose by three and a half pence. The exchange rate announced by the Central Bank was stable for both English and American currencies. The customs gold unit rose by five li. The posted price of standard gold rose to one thousand one hundred and forty-three yuan and nine jiao. The over-the-counter pre-market transaction rose to thirty-eight yuan to eight yuan and a half. Fuxing Yong took advantage of the high price to supply, and Yisheng and other companies gradually moved in to trade. The morning opened high, but immediately fell back due to too many sellers. The exchange rate announced by HSBC was stable for both English and American currencies. At this time, the situation was stable and hovering. The silver balance tax rose by half a point. Sellers were still enthusiastic and continued to fall. However, there were still many who maintained their positions by taking advantage of the low prices. After the opening of cash, it once rose again. The exchange rate hardened, and those who liquidated their positions remained brave and continued to fall downstream due to a lack of buyers. However, after the low point, there was still cash opening. The overall trend hovered at noon. In the afternoon, the large bearish players entered the market and exerted pressure. The selling atmosphere was strong again. The supply in the market exceeded demand and gradually went downstream. It once fell to a low price of one thousand one hundred and thirty-three yuan and a half. Buyers began to move, and the central bank continued to open cash and rose again. The Indian silver report increased by two annas. Many people still posted two yuan and six jiao to take advantage of the high price to sell. The daily market situation is recorded below.

The opening price in the morning was one thousand one hundred and thirty-eight yuan and three jiao, an increase of one yuan and one jiao compared to the previous closing. Yuan Mao Yong Da Decheng Dingkang Jiu Da Shengyuan Yong Fuxing Yong sold in succession, falling to seven yuan and six jiao. Da Fa Yong Da Decheng slightly advanced, rising to seven yuan and eight jiao. The exchange rate announced by HSBC was stable for both English and American currencies. At this time, the situation was hovering. The silver balance tax was announced to shrink by half a point. Da Decheng Qia Feng Yongheng Yuanyuan Mao Yong Da Feng Heng Fuxing Yong Tong Yu Run sold their strips in succession, retreating to seven yuan. Da Decheng Da Fa Yong Futai Heng bought strips taking advantage of the low price, rising to seven yuan and seven jiao. The exchange rate hardened, and the people's hearts were shaken. Floating profits were liquidated. Chun Yuan Yong Tongfu Tong Yu Run Hui Xiang Ding Feng sold together, falling to six yuan and six jiao. Fuxing Yong Hui Xiang Futai Heng advanced, rising to seven yuan and four jiao. Fuxing Yong Da Fa Yong sold strips. The closing price at noon was one thousand one hundred and thirty-seven yuan, and the situation was stable after the closing.

The opening price in the afternoon was one thousand one hundred and thirty-six yuan and nine jiao. Da Decheng Gan Changxiang Tong Feng Heng Yicheng Yuanyi Ding Kang Qingfa Yong Heng Yuanyuan Chang Yong and others competed to sell, retreating to five yuan and one jiao. Futai Yong Da Decheng Qia Feng Yong Shengyuan Yong slightly advanced taking advantage of the low price, rising to five yuan and a half. Tongtai Chang Hongli Heng Jiqun Yicheng Fuxing Yong Zhichang Da Decheng Fuyu sold in succession, and fell to three yuan and a half. Chun Yuan Yong Qia Feng Yong Yuan Mao Yong Futai Heng Ruixing Qingfa Yong Dingkang bought in succession taking advantage of the low price, rising to five yuan and six jiao. Da Decheng Heng Yu Dingkang sold taking advantage of the high price, retreating to four yuan and four jiao. The Indian silver report increased by one and three annas. Qia Feng Yong Shengyuan Yong Chun Yuan Yong Gan Changxiang Da Decheng Futai Heng advanced together, rising to five yuan and three jiao. Yuanyi Da Fa Yong Shang sold. The closing price was one thousand one hundred and thirty-five yuan and one jiao. The situation was stable after the closing.

Causes and Consequences of Recent Fluctuations in Standard Yarn and Cotton Over the Past Month

Recently, the market conditions of standard yarn and cotton have been declining in a straight line, and the declining trend has become increasingly intense and fierce. In early March, favorable rumors circulated, and financial institutions, gold merchants, and securities firms absorbed large quantities, resulting in the highest price at the opening on April 14. The peak of September standard yarn reached 213.1 yuan, only 0.3 yuan lower than the merchant price on December 4 of the previous year. The peak of August standard cotton was 46 yuan, which was 0.1 yuan higher than the high price on December 4 of the previous year. Subsequently, due to sluggish real sales and weak purchasing power from customers, the daily increase in yarn inventory in yarn warehouses exceeded 31,000 bales. Although financial institutions invested and worked hard to purchase standard cotton, the transportation of coarse cotton from various routes to Shanghai increased the inventory to 80,000 to 90,000 dan. At this time, factories lacked sufficient needs for this coarse cotton. At the same time, the Indian cotton purchased by Chinese and foreign factories arrived in Shanghai one after another, with more than 50,000 pieces. Factories can use it temporarily, and there is no urgent need to purchase raw materials. Therefore, the cotton market turned sharply downward, and the cotton market weakened, and the yarn market became even more depressed. The biggest reason is that the smuggling in North China is becoming more and more prosperous, which has a great impact on cotton yarn. Although there is no actual cloth transported in large quantities, the sales of yarn have been greatly reduced. According to the investigation, at this time last year, the purchase of various yarns in the north was as much as 12,000 bales. Therefore, general short sellers were very active, and drastic changes occurred. The market fell sharply. Standard yarn fell sharply by 10.07 yuan in the near month and 11.5 yuan in the far month compared with the high price on April 14. Standard cotton fell sharply by 2.65 yuan in the near month and 3.2 yuan in the far month. The recent high and low prices of standard yarn and cotton are excerpted below.

Shen Bao Literary and Art Special Issue

A'fa

— Jiang Jing

A long time ago, the villagers said that the yellow cow was A'fa's wife.

Many people asked A'fa: "Did you marry the yellow cow as your wife?" But A'fa, as always, opened his small eyes hostilely, snorted, and walked away.

No one knew where A'fa was from or what his background was; he had been here for more than ten years and was now in his fifties. It was said that he came as a beggar at first, and then found odd jobs to do, so he settled down. The year before last, he had a serious illness and could no longer work, so he had to work as a cowherd at Ru De Gong's house.

He was short and thin, with many scars on his scabby head; a particularly large one was on his right cheek, pulling his face tightly and distorting it. His eyes were as small as a mouse's, but when he looked at people, they flashed with a snake-like vicious light; his nostrils were very flat, as if they had been pressed by something. This ugly and humble appearance and the dirty color gave people a disgusting impression. "This guy must have been conceived by a monkey, or else he was scraped out of some latrine." People joked about him like this, not treating him as a human being; naughty children even gave him the nickname "monkey spawn" and often shouted it behind his back recklessly.

A'fa never resisted the contempt, ridicule, or even insults of others with actions or words; he always avoided eye contact and remained silent, only a vicious and resentful light flashed in his dark eyes, as if his heart was being tormented by some poison. He would immediately walk away quietly, never looking back, as if ashamed to stand with them. Some people said that he used to fight and scold people, but he suffered too much, and then he became like this.

But people ridiculed and insulted him even more because of this, and at the same time, they all hated him. No one regarded him as a companion or a friend, and no one said a word to him that should be said between people; they just made fun of him.

"Our Brother A'fa... Haha..."

A'fa never interacted with people and never spoke to them; he only used the simplest questions and answers with his master, Ru De Gong! "What? Yes, um." It seemed that A'fa thought that humans were all malicious animals that could not be approached. He not only deliberately avoided everyone, but also deliberately avoided everything related to people; his ugly face was always rigid, and no human expressions of joy, anger, sorrow, or happiness could be found. People couldn't guess what his heart was like.

However, he showed some kindness to me exceptionally. There were quite a few opportunities for conversations between us, but his words were always very short, no more than five or six sentences at most.

Once, I [missing text] people's opinions. He stared at me silently for a while, and then said coldly in a firm tone:

"They are all... ghosts! They can't afford me, and I despise them even more!"

In this world, the only thing he loved was that yellow cow. He cut grass, bathed it, caught lice for it, and washed its eyes with cold water every day. He did these things with great effort and was so happy that he often hummed some tunes that he himself didn't know.

The cow grew fatter and stronger day by day, but he answered people's praise for it with angry eyes.

He couldn't leave his cow for a moment. He had to follow it when plowing the fields; he always looked at it with eyes full of infinite affection, and sometimes he would smile ecstatically. When herding the cow, he was not with others. He took it to places where no one was and returned very late. But this caused even more rumors, and people said in [missing text] tones:

"Our Brother A'fa is still a virgin!"

But all the rumors and laughter did not harm his feelings for the cow in the slightest.

One summer evening, I saw A'fa and the cow on the edge of the mulberry forest by the field where no one could see them; at this time, the fields were quiet and there was no one there, only the sound of the cow eating grass could be heard. A'fa stood next to the cow, looking at it quietly with a greedy look, sometimes smiling, as if he was having some sweet memories. He often stroked the cow's back and neck gently—stroking it for a long time, making a low, blurred, intoxicated sound in his throat. The cow seemed very comfortable, raised its head, and wagged its tail obediently; at this time, A'fa laughed hee hee.

"Um, you [missing text]—" He patted it gently on the back: "What is it for? Eat."

But the cow started to eat the crops in the field. A'fa anxiously lifted its mouth and tapped its nose with his fingers, teaching it like a child:

"Um, you... why are you so greedy? It's better to eat grass." He stared at it, with an unspeakable enthusiasm in his eyes. "Um, eat! What good tender grass!" He smiled.

But the yellow cow still wanted to eat the crops. It [missing text] A'fa argued; A'fa pulled it hard, and the yellow cow shook its head and kept panting.

"Hey, hey, what are you doing? —What?" A'fa became anxious and raised the cow's mouth high again: "Are you angry with me? —" His voice became dejected, and his face showed a painful expression: "Are you angry with me? Are you? —Why?"

The cow didn't [missing text] shake its head anymore, but tried hard [missing text] to shrink its neck back, its nostrils [missing text] ; "Are you really angry with me?" His voice [missing text] was completely trembling. He suddenly [missing text] his hand and cried.

At first, he covered his face and sobbed, but soon he put down his hand and picked up the cow rope again. The cow lowered its head and didn't eat the crops, like a person regretting something. At this time, A'fa suddenly became happy and laughed ecstatically. He squatted down and smelled its nose, and stroked its eyes:

"Okay," he said, "let's make peace, and everyone don't be angry. —Here, eat, or you'll be hungry!" He wiped his tears while smiling.

Last year, Ru De Gong sold the yellow cow without A'fa's knowledge. When A'fa knew that his beloved yellow cow had left him forever, he was stunned and shed tears silently. A month later, he also died.

Trembling Heartstrings

— Jiang Jiping

Paper Flowers

The weather is so sunny that it is very pleasant, but there is a bit of wind, which is a bit of a regret in spring. There is also a lot of wind in the yard, but this wind is definitely not as uncomfortable as the wind in winter. This wind seems to have a bit of poetry. When you hear the sound of this wind, you will think of the ancient poet's line: "The spring breeze is ten miles of Yangzhou Road." Although the spring breeze now will not be so gentle, it can always make people feel a little drunk. Although there are only a few old clothes drying in the yard, when they are swayed by the breeze, that kind of posture under the spring sun feels an indescribable beauty. The children tore up a lot of red and green handmade paper, a pile here and a few pieces there, which really looks a bit like the remnants of flowers and fallen leaves that have been destroyed by wind and rain and fallen on the ground. After a while, the wind blew the paper scraps on the ground to the two pots of dead branches of the rose flowers. From a distance, the red paper scraps are sandwiched in the middle of the rose branches, which really looks like the dead roses are blooming again. I am very happy in my heart, although I know it is fake, but then what in the world is not fake, but this kind of happy feeling is always rare.

Thinking of Magnolia

I don't know why I suddenly thought of magnolia, and also thought of things from a long time ago. At that time in Qingdao, I went to the trestle bridge in the evening. The person walking in front was one of my female classmates, with two magnolias slanted in her hair. The wind was warm, and the fragrance of the magnolias evaporated. The feeling at that time was as if I had just opened a bottle of very good port wine, and smelled the mouth of the bottle. I was already a little intoxicated without drinking it in my mouth. We got off the trestle bridge and walked on the beach again. We sat quietly on the stones and looked at the lights across the bank. Facing a blue expanse, we looked at the distant market of cold stars on the other side. The emotions in our hearts immediately became tense, and the line "Two or three sparks are Guazhou" jumped in my mind again. That was already five years ago. Where has she gone now? Who knows? Why can't this scene at the time be erased? The sun has already set in the west, and a faint golden color is spread on the floor. For some reason, the room is different from the past. The books on the bookshelf and the books on the desk, I don't know who arranged them so neatly, and the calligraphy and paintings on the wall also seem much cleaner than in the past. Is it happy? There is also a bit of lonely disappointment. Zheng Banqiao's poem on the small strip hanging on the wall: "The heavy snow fills the world, why do you travel with a sword? If you want to talk about your heart, go to the tavern together." After reading this heroic poem, it seems that I should cheer up a bit, but I always feel weak and powerless. The setting sun is shining through the window, and the curtains are shaking gently. I feel like I have lost something, and I always feel a little disappointed.

Talking about "Mass Recitation"

— Quan Lin

The countries where "mass recitation" first became popular were the Soviet Union and Germany. The first person to introduce it to the United States was M. Goldt, who believed that this was the most powerful method in mass culture and a most practical art. In his published "A Collection of Twelve Million Ones," he collected several pieces of this kind of material. He worked hard to promote this movement in the United States and encouraged American writers to write more of this kind of literature.

The form of "mass recitation" is like this: using the most concise and stimulating words, it is written into a kind of short and powerful operatic form of duet, chorus, and solo, and performed by a number of people (about twenty or at most thirty) together with music. This must be singable and fit the concise musical rhythm. Needless to say, each sentence must be very short and have the power of a bullet. Reading it out forcefully and unhurriedly with correct and clear articulation, so that every word can convey a kind of stimulation to the audience, of course, some exciting materials are needed here, so some realistic romantic components are necessary.

The biggest feature of "mass recitation" is that the actors do not have to perform entirely on stage. Several actors wear the same clothes as the audience and mix among the audience. There is no need for makeup and painting faces. Their task is to chorus or shout loudly offstage. To give an example, in Goldt's "Strike," a "wealth" and a "poverty" are dueting on stage.

Wealth (with a face obsessed with inner desires, a fat person)—Who are you? Have you ever been invited?

Poverty—(A ragged woman) (calmly) I have not been invited.

Wealth—Then why are you here? Get out! You dirty woman!

Poverty—I am poverty, your sister, wherever you go, I go.

Wealth—(Angrily) Nonsense! Nonsense! Poverty is not my sister.

Poverty—(Calmly) Greed is our father.

Wealth—(Shouting) Get out! Ragged woman! My brother calls

Poverty—(Coldly) You are used to dealing with me in this way! ...

Here, the men are a unit, the women are another unit, and the chorus of many people is another unit. Later, a young leader is discovered in the crowd, and he duets with those on and off the stage. At the end, several actors offstage rush onto the stage from the side of the stage. This scene of "mass recitation" ends in a tragic and uplifting shout and chorus.

This method obviously gives the audience a great stimulus. They often instinctively become one with the actors and shout along with them. Goldt once said this about the performance of that "Strike":

"The audience was surprised: they didn't know who these people sitting next to them were—they were shouting and singing here and there—the sound of the drama seemed to come from the people next to them. So the workers and those people joined together and shouted exciting slogans and rushed to the side of the stage. The audience was gradually surrounded by the excitement around them. They became one of the actors, they became the 'real masses' in the drama. At the end of that 'mass recitation,' everyone in the pool was shouting."

Let's think about how tragic and uplifting that scene was! What an effective literature this is!

The second feature of mass recitation is that it is very simple. At first glance, it seems troublesome to need twenty or thirty actors and music, but it is unexpectedly simple! First, it does not need a magnificent stage and scenery. Any gathering place of the masses can be used, even outdoors, as long as there is a simple stage and a few tables and benches. Second, except for two or three people who play nobles, police, etc., who need simple makeup, all the other actors do not need makeup or costume changes. This is easier to plan than Tai Fuxi's "open-air drama."

Regarding music, it is naturally best to have it, but I think Chinese music is very underdeveloped, or only a violin or piano is enough for the first trial performance.

This kind of "mass recitation" needs a very energetic director, whose task is even more important than the director in a drama. The actors must carefully memorize and match the very correct rhythm and spacing. The director must pay attention to avoiding confusion due to excessive excitement—this is easy to offend in the first trial performance.

The third feature of mass recitation is that it can unite the strong will of the audience (Saedarilz). It is like a powerful speech. It can uniformly motivate the audience. There is no individualism, no leading actor and supporting actor, every actor is equally important. And more meaningful is that it can turn this performance into the audience's own performance and turn this "mass recitation" into the masses' own thing. What a powerful way to make backward masses accept the mission of literature and art!

Daughter-in-law

— Hua Sha

Early morning—it was the early morning of my third day in Nantou Town. The sun had just emerged from the red glow on the horizon, behind the village on the opposite bank of the river, its fat face flushed. The fields were calm and clear, and although it was early spring, people already felt comfortable and warm.

I don't know how many wheelbarrows, piled high with firewood and tree roots, "creaked, rumbled!" as they heavily rolled down from the small stone bridge on the left and passed in front of the school gate. In such a beautiful early morning, I took a pair of overshoes covered in mud and walked towards the river. The muddy yellow river water slowly flowed downstream. A small, thin woman stood on a square stone that was exposed to the surface of the water, holding two pieces of wet clothes. She was laboriously crossing from the square stone to the river beach, slowly climbing ashore, looking as if she was about to fall. Her hair was frighteningly disheveled on her face, so that people could only see her flat nose and pouting little mouth. When she was about to stand up straight, she saw me and smiled at me strangely, revealing her big yellow teeth:

"Are you washing your shoes? Um, um, you are welcome to come and play at my house when you have time!"

The woman spoke to me unexpectedly. I thought she might be the mother of a primary school student in the school, or perhaps she was a postpartum woman who had just given birth. So I smiled and asked her:

"Then where is your home?"

She pointed with the stick in her hand and said, "It's over there."

My gaze followed her stick and I saw a rectangular thatched house on that side:

"Oh! I'll come to see you when I'm free."

She walked away without looking back, separating her bare little feet and walking as slowly as a cart driver pushing a cart.

From then on, whenever I walked past the door that the woman had pointed out, I paid attention to her. She always sat on the small wooden stool in front of the door, cleaning some vegetables or washing clothes, her movements were slow, and she was always [missing text]. Moreover, she never raised her face.

Soon, I finally found an opportunity to see the woman and a twelve or thirteen-year-old girl digging in the mud in the square, looking for something in the mud and throwing it towards the wax-yellow ducklings. The ducks were staggering and scrambling. The girl used a pair of bamboo chopsticks to clamp something and threw it to where the woman was sitting. I really wanted to know what they were doing, so I walked up to her; I only saw many earthworms crawling beside her feet, but she lowered her head as if she hadn't spoken to me, picking the earthworms into sections and then throwing them at the ducks. Her hands were dirty and greasy, ignoring how the earthworms wriggled on her fingers, and still shaking her wooden-like arms as she picked them up.

"Hey! Aren't you afraid of goosebumps doing this?" She didn't seem to hear my words.

"Can't you just give them the whole thing to eat?"

She still didn't answer me, but lowered her head even more, her bare toes moving restlessly in the mud.

I didn't know why she was so indifferent as she slowly paced around the square. A little duck stretched its neck, shook its head, and half an earthworm hung outside its mouth. Seeing this, the girl called out angrily, "You stupid woman! Don't pick them shorter! I'll tell Mom!" But I didn't see the girl move, so I strode out of the square.

After that, I saw the woman every day, holding a small bamboo pole and sitting on the bank of the river opposite, her feet hanging over the river, the river water slowly flowing under her feet. A flock of goslings pecked at the green grass on the grass beside her. Sometimes I saw the woman swinging her feet as if admiring the beauty of nature, gently tapping the grass with the bamboo pole, sometimes staring fixedly at the house opposite. When I walked back to my residence across the small wooden bridge every day, I would definitely pass by her side, and because I had never received her answer, although I really wanted to ask her, I never did.

A few days passed again. One day, when I was walking next to her, she smiled at me again and asked me:

"Are you going back?"

"Yes, going back," I said, pausing slightly beside her. Suddenly she pointed to the school opposite and said:

"What are you doing there?"

"Teaching," I said.

She looked up at me, and smiled again in disbelief and fear. At this time, from her legs with her trousers rolled up high, I saw patches of blue-purple and bloodstains. The instep of her feet was shiny and swollen, and her neck was full of scratches. It was clear that she had been injured. So I thought again that in her blue rag clothes, there might be more scars that I wouldn't see. So I asked:

"What's on your legs?"

She frowned at me, and then replied indifferently:

"The mother-in-law hit me."

"What about on your neck?"

"The girl scratched me."

"Where is your husband?"

"Gone."

From her simple answer, I couldn't hear any resentment or pain. I was surprised by her indifferent expression. I wanted to know what she needed.

"Have you had lunch?"

"I don't eat it."

"Do you have any copper coins..."

"Copper coins..."

"Have you ever been to the street?"

"Street..."

"Do you want to go to the city to play?"

"City..."

She repeated the two words as if she had never heard these words before, and she was thinking. Her voice "um um" in my ears like a fly, making people annoyed. Finally I said:

"The sun is going down soon, aren't you going back?"

"The girl hasn't come to call me yet." At this time, she was gently tapping the grass with the bamboo pole again, showing a very naive appearance.

A girl quickly ran from the opposite bank, this girl was the one I had seen in the square that day. She shouted before crossing the small bridge:

"Stupid woman! Go home!" The woman shrugged her shoulders in horror, slowly climbed up from the river bank, and took a pole with the girl and "Go go!" The geese were driven across the small bridge and went home.

Tomorrow, that woman and the geese would no longer appear on the other side of the river. I was surprised, I was shocked, and I deliberately walked back and forth in front of the woman's thatched house. The geese and ducks were still walking slowly in the square, the girl was still digging in the mud, but only the woman was missing. I wondered where she had gone.

It wasn't until evening that I saw the woman again, her forehead bandaged with a dirty cloth, blood flowing from the cloth layer on her forehead to her face. She used the bamboo pole for driving the geese to support her body, stumbling out of the thatched house. Her face was gray-yellow and swollen, and her feet moved forward like two thick pieces of wood. Suddenly, a woman in her forties or fifties rushed out of the thatched house, grabbed the stupid woman's shoulder, pulled her back fiercely, and said, "You dare to go out." The stupid woman fell to the ground. Stepping forward, I said to the old woman, "Why do you have to pull her like that?"

The old woman tilted her head towards me, and said to me with a more stern face:

"Miss, you have your business, this is not something you can manage. My daughter-in-law is a stupid woman, and she peed on the new bed three days after entering the house. Everyone in the town knows that."

"Since you know she's stupid, don't hit her. It's not right to hit her," I said.

"Hum! You know how to talk. I work hard to weigh firewood and can't earn much money, and you can send her to you to raise her," the woman said, dragging the stupid woman towards me, and shouting: "You can raise her, and I won't say anything else." I angrily pointed at the old woman and cursed "bastard," and then quickly walked out of the square.

Lessons from the Fall of Abyssinia

— Xiaoshan

The country of Abyssinia, with an area of only 900,000 square kilometers and a population of only 5,500,000 (in fact, the Abyssinian race has only 3 million people), supported its sacred war of resistance for seven months, but ultimately failed. On May 5th, the Abyssinian capital fell, and the fascist Mussolini's army of the imperialists finally occupied the entire country.

However, we dare not grieve for Abyssinia, but we have learned several lessons from this war. The first is the mutual exclusion and aggression between imperialists. The League of Nations, supported by Britain, disintegrated invisibly, and the "collective security" that once caused a sensation has now completely become a bubble. Following the development of this condition, the period of great tragedy for humanity is approaching even more urgently. But we don't need to be afraid, the pain of the imperialists themselves is unimaginable, and it cannot be compensated by obtaining one or two colonies, just as Italy's invasion of Abyssinia mobilized the whole country, sacrificing money, lives, and property. Even if they get Abyssinia, their vitality cannot be restored. Therefore, the great tragedy of humanity will unfold even more seriously. The second lesson is that the weak nations of the world all understand that sacred struggle is great and will be victorious. The reason for Abyssinia's failure is of course material backwardness and being outnumbered. A small, unassisted country can still withstand eight months of imperialist massacre, and the whole country is united, resisting until the entire country is tragically submerged. This shows how great the wars of small and weak nations are. If the small and weak nations of the world, based on this profound lesson, form a great iron fortress, we believe that the imperialists, even in eight years... cannot subdue the small nations of the world.

Looking back at our China, we have an area of 11,173,558 square li and a population of 450 million, which is far different from Abyssinia. The population of Abyssinia is only the population of Shanghai, and it can resist for eight months. Therefore, the lesson we learned from Abyssinia is that Abyssinia's failure is glorious. They died for struggle, they perished for struggle. We must accept this great lesson!

Special Feature

Mr. Lu and Mr. Ye Detail the Invention Process of the Rotary Tri-Purpose Light Bulb

— Yu

Messrs. Lu Zhongwen and Ye Liang, our countrymen, have invented a "rotary tri-purpose light bulb" that is different from ordinary ones. Yesterday afternoon, the reporter visited them, and they told us a lot about the invention process.

Messrs. Lu and Ye were originally engineers at a foreign merchant's light bulb factory. After resigning, they felt that the existing light bulbs were simple and not durable. After more than two years of careful research, they successfully tested the "rotary" light bulb.

The "rotary tri-purpose light bulb" has two types. One type has three filaments inside the bulb, each emitting a different light intensity. The top filament is 5 candlepower, the middle filament is 25 candlepower, and the bottom filament is 50 candlepower. The key to changing the light intensity is a specially made rotating copper head. When it is inserted, it is 5 candlepower. When rotated, the second filament lights up, changing it to 25 candlepower. When rotated again, the third filament lights up, changing it to 50 candlepower. This is like buying three light bulbs of different intensities.

There is also another type, which also has three filaments, but all three filaments have the same light intensity. When the first filament breaks, simply rotate the special copper head, and the second filament can still emit light. When the second filament breaks, rotate the copper head again, and the third filament can still emit light. It cannot be used until both filaments are broken. In this way, it is as if one light bulb is used as three light bulbs.

There are two complete models of the light bulb, which are placed in the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing for registration. The only one that I was able to see was a light bulb that had not yet been fitted with a copper head. The glass shell was flat and round, and there were three filaments inside the glass shell, top, middle, and bottom. As for the copper head? It is said to be completely different from ordinary ones, with a thick texture and a spiral shape. There are four protruding feet at the bottom that are embedded in the glass shell, so that it will not be impossible to insert it during rotation. At the top of the copper head, the ordinary ones have two egg-shaped tin blocks, while theirs have three very small tin points. There is also a hook-shaped thing next to it, and the change of the filament during rotation happens on it. The color of the copper head is chrome-plated.

Later, there will also be a two-purpose light bulb, which can change between two light intensities.

In terms of price, because the structure is slightly more complicated and the cost is higher, the selling price will be slightly more expensive than ordinary ones. It is probably above 30 cents and below 40 cents. The two-purpose one may be cheaper.

The electricity consumption is the same as ordinary ones, and perhaps a wattmeter will be used to test it for everyone in the future.

This "rotary tri-purpose light bulb" has been applied to the Ministry of Industry for a five-year patent. Cantonese merchant Mr. Chen Weizhou has invested in setting up the "Central Tri-Purpose Light Bulb Factory" on Rue Sa-po-sai, with a total capital of 90,000 yuan in the first phase. It has now ordered light bulb making machines from the China Rongchang Factory.

In terms of raw materials, except for the filaments and copper heads, which are American goods, the rest are domestic goods.

The assembly of the machines will be completed in about two weeks. Formal business must wait until there is a considerable inventory. The future measurement is four to five thousand pieces per day.

The main production processes in their factory are as follows: core,燙鈎[unknown], 綳絲 [unknown], medicinal powder, sealing, exhausting air, 校光 [unknown], copper head, stamping, final light inspection, packaging.

Finally, Messrs. Lu and Ye led me to see the factory building that was being assembled, which was a small Western-style building, all the way up and down. The craftsmen were still working hard, and some small machines were already placed there.

After leaving, I felt very happy, because it is always a good thing for our countrymen to invent more, no matter how big or small!

Cotton-Picking Women

— Dongguang

In mid-September, the sorghum and corn were harvested. On the ochre land, there were only patches of snow-like cotton fields. In summer, the stems of the cotton seedlings are dark purple. The autumn wind blows the leaves yellow, and they roll and fly on the plains. The stems and branches also turn ochre. The bolls open like small bird claws, grasping handfuls of white flowers. Under the gray sky, it is unexpectedly spacious. In each cotton field, there is a small woven grass hut, and there is an elderly farmer who is loyal to his duty. He wears a white sheepskin robe, holds a pipe like a stone statue, and patrols the edges of the land with a clumsy musket on his back, guarding the harvest for the owner...

The night, accompanied by the barking of dogs, drifted across the bank of the small river. The water flowed gurglingly under the single-plank bridge. The ferry boat glided across the river and drifted back and forth. At this time, groups of women picking cotton returned. They carried bulging, huge bundles on their backs, bending their bodies, and moved under the bundles, walking in rows from the field ridges. Along the river slope, they walked to the head of the wooden bridge, happily threw the large cotton bales to the ground, raised their faces and breathed a sigh of relief, and sat down on the cotton bales. They waited for the ferry to row across the shore with a creaking sound. They hobbled on their pointy feet, dragged the large cotton bales onto the boat, and then squatted down happily, asking each other about the weight and price:

"How many coppers per ten catties do you get from picking for Sanxingtang?"

Page 20

"Two big coppers (i.e., four small coppers)."

"We get three and a half small coppers. I won't pick for the Ma family tomorrow."

Mr. Zhang Shutong's Recent Work (Yu Mountain Scenery)

These are all young women and girls. In autumn, small households finish their own work, and the men go to the wilderness to collect firewood. The women go to pick cotton for the landlords. They go to the cotton fields from the end of July to pick "one spray" (that is, when the entire cotton field is full of cotton) and then "one spray" again. They work hard, wiping away large beads of sweat, under the scorching sun and in the early autumn evening wind, busy without wanting to say a word of idle talk, until it gets dark. Then they carry large bundles of cotton bales on their backs—all picked by their non-stop hands that day. Although it is so heavy that it bends their backs, they are not afraid of it at all. Sometimes they even hate that it is not heavier. — Crossing the river, a group of women are followed by the "manager" of the landlord's family, a gentle gentleman in a long gown, holding a pair of shiny walnuts or a snuff bottle in his hand.

They jumped off the boat, carried their own bundles, and dragged themselves across a stretch of sand, panting with difficulty, and climbed the slope. The lights in the village were on, and the smoke from the cooking fires permeated the stars in the sky. A group of people walked towards the Ma family in the south of the village, and another group turned past the stockpiling yard—a red warning light had been lit on the mountain-like salt pile.

They were like a batch of flood victims, a dark, dense line, walking along the tall white lime wall, entering the gate of Sanxingtang, and carrying the cotton to be weighed according to the bamboo slips they received. The cotton bale was lowered from the large frame scale. The plumb line hit there, and the scale lever was raised high. The cotton-picking woman could only open her two fiery eyes and sigh, not daring to make a sound, waiting for the young man who pulled the scale lever to shout:

"Seventy catties!"

"I only have seventy catties?"

"How much? A hundred catties? Add you too."

Silently accepting the two sarcastic remarks, the accountant gave her the money, took back the slip, and another old witch-like woman came over and pulled her aside to search her pants to see if she had stolen a ball of cotton. After the search, she was quickly chased out of the gate.

On the way home, they counted the copper coins one by one, forgetting their fatigue and humiliation, thinking that the day's work was done, they could buy a foot of cloth, a large cake, or a packet of needles and a bundle of thread for the children or the younger brothers, always kind, simple, and spending a string of difficult days in the future.

Sending Away the Dull Spirit

— Fangzhou

—Gleanings of Local Customs—

The eastern half of the sky was burned red by the sun just climbing out of the horizon. A layer of golden brilliance had been sprinkled on the pine forest in front of the hillside. The warm air gradually surrounded Double Pagoda Village, and the water in the river beside Lotus Leaf Ridge was flowing quietly.

At breakfast time, a burst of noisy shouting and yelling came from the stone road in the distance. The village dogs were barking madly, jumping from east to west, as if they were crazy. This tranquil village was suddenly stirred up with unrest and commotion, and the noise was getting closer and closer, as if to shatter people's eardrums.

"They are sending away the dull spirit for Mo Afu's wife!" A'cai said, holding his rice bowl.

"Don't go out, don't go and bump into the dull spirit!" A'cai's mother told everyone not to go to watch, because if anyone bumped into the dull spirit, they would go mad like Mo Afu's wife—smashing furniture and hitting people.

However, the edge of the well in front of the teahouse and the area beneath the severed pagoda were eventually filled with a crowd of people, men, women, old, and young, all standing on tiptoe and looking towards the stone road.

Beside the bluestone bridge on the stone road, there was a cluster of young men, rushing together with "哗啦! 哗啦!" sounds. A large bronze gong was being struck with "瞠! 瞠!" sounds, hitting with the force of an earth tremor. Two young men were carrying a broken firewood enclosure, with Mo Afu's wife tied up like a piglet and put inside. Everyone crowded around, rocking and swaying her as they ran. In the mountains, beside the fields, along the streams they ran. Running, they would relentlessly shake the enclosure, sometimes rolling it down the mountainside at the mid-point of the slope, and then carrying it and running again after it rolled to flat ground, causing Mo Afu's wife to feel a terror as if the sky was collapsing and the earth was turning upside down, and great distress.

Broadcasting

National Studies

Hu Zhangzhao, "Analects - Learning"

Transportation (1300) 9:30 PM to 10 PM last night

The Master said, "While his father is alive, observe his intentions; when his father is dead, observe his actions. If for three years he does not alter from the way of his father, he may be called filial."

Youzi said, "In the practice of ritual, harmony is prized. The way of the former kings prized this, and it was followed in all matters, great and small. Yet there is something that should not be done. To know harmony and yet to seek only harmony without regulating it by ritual, this is not permissible either."

Youzi said, "When trustworthiness is close to righteousness, words can be fulfilled. When courtesy is close to ritual, one keeps far from shame and disgrace. When one relies on those he should rely on, one can also have someone to rely on." The Master said, "The gentleman seeks not satiety in his food nor ease in his dwelling; he is diligent in his work but careful in his words. By associating with those who possess the Way, he rectifies himself. This may be called love of learning indeed."

Suzhou Ballad Singing

He Zifang and He Qinfang, Double Pearl Phoenix

China-West (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "Huo Dingjin's Private Hanging"

Pitiful cries call out to my husband in distress. My throat is choked, my mouth is mumbled. First I call "brother," then I slowly call "husband." People say I am crying for my aunt's husband. Fortunately, the two words "aunt's husband" are almost the same. I heard that we will meet on the third day of the first lunar month. I will be able to see you in the back garden. For more than a hundred days, my heart has been simple and filial. For you, I am willing to be a lowly slave. For you, I abandon my mother, and my heart is most bitter. For you, I was bewitched by the stolen Double Pearl Phoenix. Changed my surname, knelt down, and called you by your pet name. For you, I wandered in a foreign land, accompanied by a bookboy. For you, I never thought that you would achieve great success in your career. Returning home, there was a family feud. For you, I suffered disasters in prison. In just a few days, my life came to an end. I think my beauty is so ill-fated. In this world, ill-fated people like me are numerous. I only suffer because the literary family's thousand-year-old fire has been extinguished. I only grieve because the wife who has come from a thousand miles is mourning her husband. I still don't know that my ill fate has harmed you. I still don't know that I have burdened you and you have burdened me. Husband, I will never be a person who forgets affection when people are gone. I will never be a wife who shows no affection at all. I still remember your words before you left home. Choose a date to tie the knot. I think of you thousands of times a day. I have lost all news from Chang'an. My soul often dreams of your face. I asked a matchmaker to come to my door immediately. I hope to play the phoenix flute with you soon. I hope that your family will become famous as soon as possible. After you succeed in the imperial examinations, there will be more success. I don't think about tea and rice all day long. I cry so much that my tears flow like shuttles every day. I only said that you have forgotten our love and reason. I am willing to shave my head and recite the Buddha's name. Husband, I never knew that everything cannot be controlled by humans. My maternal uncle introduced me to another husband. From ancient times, a horse has only one saddle. A woman has never been married to two husbands. For you, I abandoned my parents in the hall. I fled secretly at night and traveled a long way. I suffered all kinds of hardships on the way. For you, I risked the capital with the crime of deceiving the emperor. For you, I was almost sitting on pins and needles. I was ordered to be an imperial envoy in Henan. The imperial envoy inspected the early three passes. Only then did I come to your spirit, and my heart lost its pain. Now, seeing your memorial tablet, I cry to death. What face do I have to go home? I will chase you to the Yellow Springs and accompany you. If you have a soul, please appear quickly. Tell me a wonderful plan for the world. I call out "brother," I cry out "husband." My broken throat can't say half a word. My crying makes three generations of ancestors cry together. The earth and grain are magical, and there are many traces of tears. My crying is endless. One cry for "young master," one cry for "husband." Even your heart of iron and stone would feel numb.

Shanghai Yuanchang Advertising Company's broadcast radio station publishes "Mimi Collection" magazine, which has now published the second issue of the third volume. The content of this issue is divided into "Suzhou Ballad Openings," "Short Essays," "Popular Songs," and "Radio Frequency Address List." It also includes "Shanghai Opera Lyrics" and several photos of Shanghai Opera masters. It is sold for 20 cents each. The annual subscription is only 2.20 yuan, and stamps can be used as cash. The station is located at No. 7 Er Rang Fang, Caishi Road, Shanghai.

Movie News

Song and Dance Film "Flying Swallow Leans on New Makeup"

Premiering Today at the Great Light

Warner Brothers is known for its song and dance films. Past works such as "Gold Diggers of Broadway," "Footlight Parade," and "42nd Street" have all been sensational. Now, their latest work, "Colleen," will premiere at the Great Light today (Friday). The male lead of the film is Dick Powell, and the female lead is Ruby Keeler, who is good at dancing. They can also be called old partners. In addition, there is the lively, round-eyed Joan Blondell, the hippie-smiling Jack Oakie, and Paul Trebe, the Broadway dance king who is as famous as Fred Astaire. With such a gathering of talents, competing to contribute their strengths, it is indeed worthy of attention. This film not only has grand song and dance scenes, but also the dance poses and the coordination of costumes are all brand new and unique. The director's design skills are also superhuman, especially in grasping the small details, naturally giving people hearty and cheerful laughter. There is also Warner's group of beautiful song and dance girls, most of them participating in the performance of new costume dances. In short, this is a new work that is rich in sound and color, and it is worth watching.

"Les Misérables" Premieres in Paris

"Les Misérables" is based on the French literary giant Hugo's masterpiece. The addition of the two golden-award-winning superstars, Fredric March and Charles Laughton, adds even more color to the film. The content is full of revolutionary frenzy, heroic blood, and is extremely tragic, enough to bring tears to even the stoniest of hearts. Starting today, it will be shown at the Paris Grand Theatre, and will be shipped to other cities after the screening. It is feared that people in Shanghai will not be able to see it again. Therefore, those who wish to see it, do not miss this last opportunity.

Lianhua Sound Film "Waves Washing Sand" Jin Yan and Zhang Zhizhi

"China Travel" Continues to Perform at the Carlton

The China Traveling Theater Troupe has been performing plays such as "Camille," "Thunderstorm," "Mei Luo Xiang," "The Lady's Fan," and "The Paint is Not Dry" at the Carlton Theater for more than ten consecutive days, setting a new record for the public performance of dramas in Shanghai. It is now heard that the Carlton Theater is satisfied with the troupe's performance, and the box office has not declined, and has asked to continue the performances. Therefore, the troupe may perform new plays that have never been performed in Shanghai, such as "Heroes and Beauties," "The Net," "Ward No. 5," and "The Unfinished Masterpiece." It is said that "The Unfinished Masterpiece" is Tang Huaiqiu's specialty. The Diantong Company's "Peach and Plum Tribulation" was adapted from this play. The popularity during the performance is expected.

Celebrity Fashion Exhibition

The "Celebrity Bi-Monthly" magazine needed photographs of the spring outfits of several of these ladies. Ma Yonghua, the photographer, invited them to the studio on Avenue Albert at the same time. Under the lights, they were dressed in various styles of spring clothing. As one shot after another was taken, we felt as if we were attending a fashion exhibition.

Huang Naishuang, a red coat, a rose-colored cheongsam, both the coat and the cheongsam having a black border; Yuan Shaomei, a floral cheongsam, looking very fresh; Ying Yin, simple, a blue cheongsam, with a black cloth around her, a small checkered coat, healthy beauty matching the plain colors; Tan Ying, appearing in a Western style, a red top, a black skirt, and a pure white coat, very lively, very excited; Yan Yuexian's attire intertwined with black and white; Qiu Jin's outfit seemed to have appeared in "Peach and Plum Blossoms Compete for Beauty", a small checkered patterned cheongsam and coat; Gu Guanjun, that kind of bright color is very suitable for that lively and clever body.

There are still a few ladies who could not come today, or perhaps they will be photographed tomorrow.

A Certain Film Organization Recruiting Male and Female Actors

A certain film organization, in order to promote new talent, has adopted an examination system to recruit actors. It has now entrusted Mr. Xu Mengsheng of the United Photoplay Service's Hong Kong Road Branch in this city to handle all registration procedures. The number of people to be recruited is ten men and ten women. Applicants must have a secondary school graduation level, be good at speaking Mandarin, and have stage experience to be qualified. Registration has already begun and will close on the 15th of this month. When registering, in addition to filling out the registration form, you must submit one recent two-inch half-length front, side, and full-body semi-side photo each. Those not accepted will be returned, and no registration fee or deposit will be charged. A prospectus is available, with two cents postage. Please request it from Mr. Xu Mengsheng at the United Photoplay Service's Hong Kong Road Branch.
